SEMESTER S5 
INTRODUCTION TO BIOMEDICAL SIGNAL PROCESSING 
Course Code 
PBEBT504 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None
 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course makes students familiarized with basics of digital signal processing & concepts of 
digital filters & its design and applications of biomedical signal processing. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Basics of biomedical signal processing: Introduction & relevance of 
biomedical signal processing. Biomedical signals –ECG, EMG, EEG, PCG, 
VAG, carotid pulse, speech signal, concurrent signals. Signal representation, 
Aliasing-Sampling theorem. Elementary signals. Classification of discrete 
signals - Energy and Power signals – periodic and aperiodic, even and odd 
signals. Discrete time systems - Properties of discrete systems. LTI system-
Impulse Response of a Linear Time-Invariant System -convolution- 
correlation - difference equation representation of discrete systems 
9 
2 
Fourier Analysis: Fourier Analysis for Continuous Time Processes-Synthesis 
of an ECG signal using pure sinusoid. Frequency Domain Analysis of 
discrete time signals: Discrete Fourier series - Discrete Time Fourier 
Transform- Discrete Fourier Transform-properties - Fast Fourier Transform- 
FFT algorithms (Radix 2)- decimation in - time - decimation in - 
frequency. 
9 
3 
Spectrum analysis & Z Transform: Spectrum analysis of bio signals – 
Introduction to parametric & non parametric methods. Z transform – ROC, 
properties of ROC, Properties of Z transform: Linearity, Time shifting, 
Scaling, Time reversal, Differentiation in Z domain, Convolution, 
8 

 
 
Correlation, Multiplication, Parseval’s relation, initial value theorem- 
rational Z transform-poles &zeros-LTI system function - inverse Z 
transform-long division-partial fraction expansion method-residue method-
convolution method. 
4 
Digital filters: Concept of digital filtering, types of digital filters. 
Comparison with analog filters. FIR filter design using Fourier series - use of 
window functions, IIR Digital Filters - Analog filter approximations - 
Butterworth approximation - Frequency transformation techniques - impulse 
invariant transformation - Matched Z transform technique- bilinear 
transformation 
10 
 
 
Suggestion on Project Topics  
 
Students are asked to form groups of maximum five members. Each group should identify a project 
on the areas specified below and choose suitable data base. Develop a methodology to implement the 
project. Develop the algorithm and code for the project  
 
Areas of Projects Topics: 
 
Filtering for removal of artefacts: Implementation of time domain Filters & Frequency 
domain filters for removal of high frequency and low frequency and periodic artefacts  
 
Event detection in biomedical signals – ECG: QRS wave detection, P wave and T wave 
detection, PPG: dicrotic notch detection - Heart sound detection- EEG rhythm detection  
 
Frequency Domain characterisation of Biomedical signal: Power spectrum density estimation 
of biomedical signals  
 
Wave shape and Waveform Complexity analysis: Normal and Ectopic beat, Arrhythmia 
analysis, Analysis of exercise ECG, Analysis of respiration

Project Assessment and Evaluation criteria (30 Marks) 
1. Project Planning and Proposal (5 Marks) 
 Clarity and feasibility of the project plan  
 Research and background understanding  
 Defined objectives and methodology  
2. Contribution in Progress Presentation and Question Answer Sessions (4 Marks) 
 Individual contribution to the presentation  
 Effectiveness in answering questions and handling feedback  

 
 
3.  Involvement in the Project Work and Team Work (3 Marks) 
 Active participation and individual contribution  
 Teamwork and collaboration  
4. Execution and Implementation (10 Marks) 
 Adherence to the project timeline and milestones  
 Application of theoretical knowledge and problem-solving  
 Final Result 
5. Final Presentation (5 Marks) 
 Quality and clarity of the overall presentation  
 Individual contribution to the presentation  
 Effectiveness in answering questions 
6. Project Quality, Innovation, and Creativity (3 Marks) 
 Overall quality and technical excellence of the project  
 Innovation and originality in the project  
 Creativity in solutions and approaches  
 
 

 
 
SEMESTER S5 
MEASUREMENTS AND INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Code 
PEEBT521 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None
 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. The basic objective of this course is to introduce the concepts of electronics measurements 
and instrumentation and to provide the comprehensive understanding of principles of 
measurement of basic circuit parameters and electrical quantities using instrumentation, to 
ensure accurate reliable data acquisition in engineering applications. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Block Schematics of Measuring Systems: Performance characteristics, 
Static characteristics, Accuracy, Precision, Resolution, Types of Errors, 
Dynamic 
Characteristics, 
Repeatability, 
Reproducibility, 
Fidelity. 
Measurement of Voltage and current: Moving Coil and Moving Iron 
types, Extension of Range-shunts and multiplierss, DC Voltmeters, D' 
Arsonval Movement, DC Current Meters, AC Voltmeters and Current 
Meters, Ohmmeters, Multimeters. 
    9 
2 
Bridges: Measurement of Resistance: Wheat Stone Bridge, Kelvin Bridge; 
Measurement 
of 
Inductance: 
Maxwell’s 
Bridge; 
Measurement 
of 
Capacitance:  Schering’s Bridge. Measurement Of Physical Parameters: 
Flow measurement, displacement meters, liquid level measurement, 
measurement of humidity and moisture, velocity, force, pressure, 
temperature- measurements, data acquisition systems. 
     9 
3 
Signal Generators: Sine wave generator, Frequency – Synthesized Signal 
Generator, Sweep frequency Generator. Pulse and square wave generators. 
     9 

 
 
Function Generators. Signal Analyzers: AF, HF Wave Analyzers, Harmonic 
Distortion, Heterodyne Wave Analyzers, Spectrum Analyzers, Power 
Analyzers, Capacitance –Voltage Meters, Oscillators. 
4 
Transducers: Classification, Strain Gauges; Force and Displacement 
Transducers, Resistance Thermometers- RTD, LVDT, Thermocouples, 
Hotwire Anemometers, Piezoelectric Transducers.  Oscilloscopes: Cathode 
Ray Tube, Vertical and Horizontal Deflection Systems, Delay lines, Probes 
and 
Transducers, 
Specification 
of 
an 
Oscilloscope. 
Oscilloscope 
measurement Techniques, Special Oscilloscopes – Storage Oscilloscope, 
Sampling Oscilloscope. 
      9

SEMESTER S5 
ADVANCED MICROPROCESSORS & MICROCONTROLLERS 
Course Code 
PEEBT522 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2.30 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBEBT 404 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Students will acquire an understanding of basic architecture of advanced microprocessors and 
microcontrollers for system development. 
2. Students will be able to design and develop microprocessor & controller-based solution for 
solving real world problems. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
8086 Microprocessor: Register organization – Architecture- Physical 
memory organization & segmentation-Signal descriptions of 8086 chip – 
General bus operation – Addressing capability- Assembler directives -
Addressing Modes - Introduction to Stack, Interrupts & Interrupt service 
routines, Minimum and Maximum mode 8086 system operation. 
9 
2 
80386 Microprocessor: Salient features of 80386 DX -Architecture and 
Signal Description- Register Organization-Memory addressing in Real 
Address mode, Protected mode, Segmentation, Paging & Virtual modes. 
Pentium - General features, pipelining and super scalar architecture. 
Introduction to multicore processors: Concept of multi core processing - 
Homogeneous and heterogeneous multicore processors -- Major issues in 
multicore processing - Internal architecture of Intel Core2 Duo (Simple block 
diagram representation only) - Technological features of IA processors. 
9 
3 
High performance RISC ARM architecture:  ARM Processor 
Fundamentals- ARM architecture - ARM7TDMI programmer’s model (basic 
level only)- Memory format – Embedded Applications. ARM based SoC- 
General features- Basic system-on-chip (SoC) architecture- System level 
interconnection – Memory organisation- SoC design approach.  
(Class Assignment/Seminar topics: SoC Interconnect Customization and 
9 

 
 
Configuration, Trade-off analysis on reconfigurable Parallelism, Case 
studies on design approach) 
Introduction 
to 
high 
performance 
computing- 
GPU 
hardware 
architecture- Comparison with CPU – GPU programming mode- GPU in 
Radiation imaging.  
4 
Introduction to ESP32 Microcontroller: Features of ESP32 development 
board – Architecture - Pin configuration – ESP32 v/s Arduino – 
Programming of ESP32 with Arduino IDE (only basic level). Introduction 
to STM32: Fundamentals of 32 -bit STM controllers – Architecture - STM 
boot modes - Interfacing of STM32 with stepper motor and 7 segment 
display. 
9

Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Introduction to nanotechnology and bio nanotechnology, time 
frame of nanobiotechnology, Biocompatibility and its assessment, Cell-
nanomaterial interactions, toxicity and environmental impact 
9 
2 
Nano particles preparation methods: Synthesis of metallic,ceramic,polymeric 
nanoparticles &its application in biofield. Biomimetic based nano structure. 
Biomolecules synthesis-DNA,viruses.Dendrimers Green synthesis methods, 
Recombinant DNA technology, Monoclonal antibodies 
9 
3 
Analytical tools in nanobiotechnology: Tools in Nanobiotechnology: 
Microscopy and imaging techniques such as SEM, TEM, AFM and STM 
Elemental composition by EDS, WDX, ICPMS, SIMS etc. Morphology and 
crystal structure by XRD and XAS. Fluorescent microscopy and confocal 
microscopy 
9 
4 
Applications of nanobiotechnology: Applications of nano-biotechnology in 
Biosensing, bioimaging for medical diagnosis, drug delivery, regenerative 
medicine . Nano-biotechnology in cancer, nanotherapeutics: gene therapy 
and immunotherapy. New materials and devices in medicine-implants and 
coatings, chemotherapy administration, nanobots. Future goals& Potential 
effects on global economics- Sustainable agriculture, sensors, nano carriers 
9

SEMESTER S5 
BIOMEDICAL OPTICS & BIOPHOTONICS 
Course Code 
PEEBT524 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min.  
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course will give an understanding of the light -tissue interactions and the different 
applications of lasers in imaging, diagnosis, and therapy.  
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Bio photonics and Tissue Optics: Overview, Light transport in Tissue-
Radiation transport theory, radiation transport model-basic parameters, 
scattering phase function, radiation transport equation, Tissue properties-
refractive indices, scattering properties, absorption properties. Optothermal 
interactions-temperature rise and tissue damage, optothermal and opto-
acoustic effects. Lasers for bio photonics: Basic laser action, laser diodes, 
CO2 lasers, Nd-YAG laser, optical fiber lasers.  
9 
2 
Bio 
imaging: 
Near 
field 
optical 
microscopy-basic 
principles, 
instrumentation-optical probes, biological applications-investigation of cell 
material, Optical Coherence tomography imaging-principles of operation, 
image generation in OCT, OCT system, Ultrahigh-Resolution Optical 
Coherence Tomography. Hologram and Medical Applications: Types of 
Hologram, Advantages & Disadvantages. 
 9 
3 
Lasers in Diagnosis: Bio photonics for blood analysis, optical inference 
and control of blood physiology – glucose sensing, haemoglobin 
oxygenation, tissue oxygen analysis- fundamentals, clinical applications of 
NIR oxygenation monitoring, early optical diagnosis of pressure ulcers- 
clinical diagnostics – evaluation of tissue blood perfusion, local tissue 
metabolism and oxygen supply, local tissue structure atrophy.  
9 

 
 
4 
Lasers in Treatment: Laser tissue welding-principles, benefits and 
limitations, mechanism of laser tissue welding-photochemical and photo 
thermal welding, therapeutic application of lasers in gastroenterology- 
lasers for destruction of tumors, lasers for lithotripsy, Lasers in restorative 
dentistry, laser ablation of hard tissues.  
9

SEMESTER S5 
VLSI DESIGN  
Course Code 
PEEBT526 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min.  
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCEBT303 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
This course aims to: 
1. Introduce the fundamentals of VLSI fabrication and the implementation of digital circuits 
using MOS transistors, covering MOSFET operation, MOS circuit design principles, including 
layout design rules and combinational logic circuits. 
2. Explore basic circuit concepts and review power dissipation in CMOS circuits, focusing on 
strategies for power reduction. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Basic IC fabrication technology: Basic fabrication steps- Wafer 
preparation, Oxidation, Diffusion, Etching process, Ion implantation 
techniques, Isolation techniques. Comparison and performance evaluation of 
bipolar and MOS technology. Fabrication process of MOS devices: NMOS 
and PMOS IC technology, CMOS n-well and p-well process.  
9 
2 
MOS transistor and geometrical effects: Structure of MOSFET, Operation 
of 
MOSFET, 
current 
– 
voltage 
characteristics, 
channel 
length 
modulation,short channel effects, narrow channel effects, scaling factors for 
device parameters. Analogy of MOSFET capacitance. MOS inverters: 
Basic circuit of NMOS inverter-voltage transfer characteristics, inverters 
with n- type MOSFET load. CMOS inverter - voltage transfer characteristics.
9 

 
 
3 
Combinational MOS logic circuits: Circuit operation of NMOS NOR & 
NAND gates, CMOS NOR & NAND gates, compound circuits using CMOS 
logic. Basic circuit concepts: sheet resistance, area capacitance, delay unit, 
inverter delays – driving large capacitive loads, super buffers. 
9 
 
 
4 
MOS circuit design processes: Stick Diagram, Layout design rules for 
MOS circuits – Lamda based rules, Layout examples of Inverter, NAND and 
NOR. Review of power dissipation in CMOS Circuits: Sources of power 
dissipation- static, dynamic and leakage power dissipation. Dynamic power 
reduction techniques - Supply voltage scaling approaches-parallelism, 
pipelining (Basic Concepts). 
9

SEMESTER S5 
ARTIFICIAL NEURAL NETWORKS 
Course Code 
PEEBT525 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs.30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course type 
Theory  
Course Objectives: 
1. Enable the student to understand the basic concepts of different types of neural networks  
2. Apply the knowledge gained to implement machine learning concepts to applications in 
Biomedical field. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Fundamental Concepts of Artificial Neural Networks: Structure of 
biological neurons relevant to ANNs– Comparison Basic building blocks of 
ANN. Activation functions, McCulloch-Pitts Neuron Model Learning Rules-
Hebbian Learning Rules, Perceptron, Delta, Competitive learning 
9 
2 
Single layer and Multilayer networks: Perceptron networks, Gradient 
descent method, Back Propagation algorithm Architecture, training 
algorithm. Counter Propagation Network, Adaptive resonance Theory, ART 
1 and ART 2 Learning, stability plasticity concept., Self-Organising feature 
maps, Kohonen network, SOM learning 
9 
3 
Associative memory networks: Algorithms for pattern association Hetero 
associative networks, Auto associative memory networks Bidirectional 
associative memory networks Energy Function. Hopfield networks. Support 
vector machines: hard-margin and soft-margin SVMs, concepts of kernels 
and feature spaces, Applications in Biomedical Engineering 
9 
4 
Convolutional 
Neural 
Networks: 
- 
Optimization 
Algorithms, 
Regularization Methods: L1 and L2 Regularization. Recurrent Neural 
Networks: RNN, LSTM, GRU. Transformers: BERT. Generative Models: 
GAN. Applications in Biomedical Engineering 
9 
 

 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 5 points) 
a. Clearly defines the problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant factors. 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 5 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 5 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
4. Conclusion (K3- 3 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, and depth of understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
● Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test understanding 
of the upcoming experiment. 
● Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of the 
theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
● Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
● Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
● Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
● Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper documentation 
of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 

 
 
● Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
● Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
● Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
● Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
● Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
● Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
● Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
● Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
● Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
● Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
● Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the subject. 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
● Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

Course Objectives:

SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Joint prosthesis-components-materials-Biomechanical analysis of joints – 
Spine, Hip, Knee-Human gait-phases-gait analysis methods-sensors- gait 
analysis-health and disease 
11 
2 
Mechanics of Hard Tissues -   structure and mechanical properties of bone - 
cortical and cancellous bones, Elasticity-stress, strain, elastic modulus, 
Poisson’s ratio, yield strength, ultimate tensile strength, failure strength, 
strain to failure, Wolff’s law of bone remodeling, models of viscoelasticity 
  Soft Tissues - Structure, functions, material properties – tendon function, 
elasticity in a tendon, models of non-linear elasticity in a tendon – 
physiological and non-physiological regimes, Davis’ law of soft tissue 
remodeling. 
11 
3

Contrast-Resolutions Obtainable With Retina Implants- Subretinal Artificial

in

Pigmentosa-

cochlear implants- Myoelectric prosthesis 
11 

 
 
4

Windkessel Simplifications-Heart as a Pump- Length –Tension Relationship 
in a Skeletal Muscle, P-V relationship in Ventricle-Model of Heart- Variable 
Capacitor model-Cardiac Cycle in P-V Plane-Iso Volumetric Contraction-
Contractility- Heart Lung Pumping Unit-Open Chest Model-Effect of Intra 
Thoracic Pressure-Modelling of intact Cardiovascular System-Cardiac 
Output under abnormal conditions-Graphical Solution.

SEMESTER S6 
PRINCIPLES OF RADIO DIAGNOSIS & RADIOTHERAPY 
 
Course Code 
PCEBT602 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Students will acquire knowledge of the physics and technology behind radiological imaging 
and radiotherapy. 
2. Students will be able to understand principles of radiation physics, including the interaction of 
radiation with matter. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Radiographic system: X-Ray production, interactions in the anode- 
Bremsstrahlung and characteristic radiations. Stationary and rotating anode 
X-ray tubes. Electrical circuit for an X-ray unit- Autotransformer, Timer, HT 
generator, rectification, filament circuit, meters, automatic exposure controls, 
generator ratings, factors influencing the X ray- spectra, beam quantity and 
quality, scattered radiation control in radiography- collimators and grids. 
9 
2 
Image receptors: CR image receptors - Photostimulable phosphor (PSP), 
PSP screen-film cassette imaging plate (IP), CR reader. Digital radiography 
(DR) image receptors- indirect conversion- phosphorescent screen- Cesium 
Iodide or Gadolinium Oxysulfide, active-matrix array (AMA)- amorphous 
silicon TFTs. Direct-capture DR-active-matrix array- amorphous selenium. 
Special Radiographic Techniques: Fluoroscopy- components of a digital 
fluoroscopy imaging system-dynamic flat-panel detector (DFPD) units and 
charge-coupled device (CCD) camera. Interventional Radiology-Digital 
9 

 
 
subtraction angiography- image formation- temporal and energy subtraction, 
Mammography- Features of a dedicated Mammography System, dental 
radiology- Intra-Oral Radiography, Panoramic Radiography and Cone beam 
CT. 
3 
Types of radio therapy--external beam radiation therapy (teletherapy), 
brachytherapy. 
Teletherapy 
sources- 
Kilovoltage 
and 
Megavoltage 
radiations- the unit of absorbed dose,percentage depth dose curves, isodose 
charts. Teletherapy machines: Kilovoltage and megavoltage X-Ray Units-
Linear Accelerators, Betatron, Cyclotron, collimators and beam direction 
devices, 
Gamma 
ray 
Units-Cobalt 
Machines. 
Radiation 
sources 
(radionuclides) 
for 
brachytherapy. 
Intensity-modulated 
radiotherapy- 
multileaf collimator, stereotactic techniques. Gamma knife, proton beam 
therapy. Therapy planning: Isodose curves and dose mapping, wedges, 
tissue compensators and intensity modulators, practical features of a 
treatment planning system. 
9 
4 
Instrumentation for Dosimetry: Ionization chambers, film dosimetry, 
thermo luminescent and optically stimulated luminescence dosimetry, 
semiconductor dosimeters. Radiation protection: Permissible doses, design 
features of radiotherapy facilities, materials used for shielding, primary and 
secondary barriers. Advisory and regulatory agencies. Introduction to 
Radiology information system (RIS): PACS, digital imaging and 
communication in medicine (DICOM). 
9

SEMESTER S6 
ELECTRICAL NETWORKS & ANALYSIS 
 
Course Code 
PEEBT631 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
GXEST104  
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Apply advanced circuit analysis techniques including mesh and node analysis, and utilize key 
network theorems to both DC and AC circuits, demonstrating problem-solving and critical 
thinking skills 
2. Analyze transient and steady-state responses of RL, RC, and RLC circuits using Laplace 
Transforms and initial condition methods, enhancing students' ability to interpret and evaluate 
circuit behavior. 
3. Design and characterize two-port networks and passive filters, integrating knowledge to 
create effective signal processing solutions. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Mesh and Node Analysis and Network Theorems: Mesh and node 
analysis of network containing independent and dependent sources. 
Supermesh and Supernode analysis. Steady-state AC analysis using Mesh 
and Node analysis. Thevenin’s theorem, Norton’s theorem, Superposition 
theorem, Reciprocity theorem, Maximum power transfer theorem. (applied 
to both dc and ac circuits having dependent source) 
9 
2 
Network Analysis: Transients - DC and sinusoidal response of RL, RC and 
RLC circuits, Initial and final conditions, Review of Laplace Transforms and 
Inverse Laplace Transforms, Transformation of basic signals and circuits 
into s-domain. Transient analysis of RL, RC, and RLC networks with 
9 

 
 
impulse, step and sinusoidal inputs (with and without initial conditions).  
3 
Transformed circuits in s-domain: Transform impedance/admittance of R, 
L and C - Transfer Function representation – Poles and zeros. Analysis of 
Coupled Circuits: – Dot polarity convention – Sinusoidal steady state 
analysis of coupled circuits - Linear Transformer as a coupled circuit - 
Analysis of coupled circuits in s-domain. 
9 
4 
Two port networks and Passive filters: Characterization of two port 
networks using Z, Y, Hybrid and Transmission parameters, Tand π 
representations. Interrelationship among parameter sets. Series and parallel 
connections of two port networks. Passive filters – Filter fundamentals, 
Classification of Filters, Characteristic impedance, Design of Constant K - 
Low Pass, High Pass & Band Pass filters. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
IOT & BIOMEDICAL APPLICATIONS 
 
Course Code 
PEEBT632 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Develop a comprehensive understanding of Internet of Things (IoT) concepts, including 
key protocols, architectural principles, and sensor technologies, with a focus on their 
theoretical applications and implications. 
2. Examine the various IoT protocols and architectures, understanding their roles and 
interactions within IoT ecosystems, and evaluating their effectiveness in different 
contexts. 
3. Explore the theoretical aspects of wearable health monitoring systems, including their 
design, functionality, and integration with data analytics and cloud technologies to 
address healthcare challenges. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to IoT and Enabling Technologies: Introduction to Internet 
of Things – Definition and Characteristics of IoT, Physical Design of IoT – 
IoT Protocols, Logical Design of IoT - IoT communication models, IoT 
Communication APIs. IoT enabled Technologies - Wireless Sensor 
Networks, Cloud Computing, Embedded Systems. Sensor Interfaces – ECG, 
EEG, PPG, Pulse Oximeter, Temperature Sensors, and Pressure Sensors. 
Challenges of using IoT in Healthcare. 
9 
2 
IoT Protocols, Architecture, and Standards: IoT Protocols & 
Architecture: Protocols - Protocol Standardization for IoT – Efforts – M2M 
and WSN Protocols – SCADA and RFID Protocols – Issues with IoT 
9 

 
 
Standardization – Unified Data Standards – IEEE802.15.4 – BACNet 
Protocol – Modbus – KNX – Zigbee. Network and Security Architecture. 
IoT Open Source Architecture (OIC) - OIC Architecture & Design 
Principles. IoT Devices and Deployment Models - IoTivity: An Open-source 
IoT Stack - Overview - IoTivity Stack Architecture - Resource Model and 
Abstraction. 
3 
Wearable Health Monitoring Systems and IoT Implementation: 
Wearable Health Monitoring System (WHMS): Basics of WHMS, Need for 
Wearable Systems, Applications of WHMS - Home Healthcare, 
Sports/Fitness. Design of Wearables: Introduction, Architecture, and 
Attributes. Design of Smart Textiles and Wearable Electronics. Issues of 
WHMS & Factors Inhibiting Growth. Building IoT with Arduino & 
Raspberry Pi: Programming – Python Program with Raspberry Pi, 
Controlling Hardware - Controlling AC Power Devices with Relays, 
Controlling Servo Motor, DC Motor. Sensors - Light Sensor, Motion 
Detection Sensors, Wireless Bluetooth Sensors. 
9 
4 
Data Handling, Analytics, and Cloud for IoT: Data Handling & Analytics: 
Introduction, Big Data, Types of Data, Characteristics of Big Data, Data 
Handling Technologies, Data Acquisition, Data Storage. Introduction to Data 
Analytics, Types of Data Analytics, Local Analytics, Cloud Analytics, and 
Applications. IoT Physical Servers and Cloud Offerings – Introduction to 
Cloud Storage Models and Communication APIs. Webserver – Web Server 
for IoT, Cloud for IoT, Python Web Application Framework, Designing a 
RESTful Web API. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
ARTIFICIAL ORGANS & IMPLANTS 
Course Code 
PEEBT633 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Students will acquire knowledge in basic principles and designing of various types of 
artificial and tissue derived implants. 
2. Students will be able to understand the use of 3D printing technology in implantation. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Cochlear implants: Basics of speech signal – Normal hearing mechanism – 
Deafness- Functional block diagram of cochlear implants-Implant 
characteristics & it’s classification -Auditory prostheses using deep brain & 
spinal cord stimulation-Physiological challenges-I/V Stimulation-Single-
multiple source systems-Real time programming. 
9 
2 
Design of artificial organs: Heart mechanism- Design of heart valves- Heart 
assist devices-Pulsatile pumping systems-Multi stage multi actuated pump 
system -Kidney and it’s artificial replacement-hemodialyzers& it’s types- 
Anatomy of skin - Design of artificial skin- Liver and it’s artificial 
replacement-The medical device market and ethical issues of implants. 
9 
3 
Micro electrode technologies for Deep Brain Stimulators (DBS): Implant 
site -Stimulation parameters - Closed loop control of DBS- Bionic micro 
stimulation- First and second generation RF powered Bionic micro 
9 

 
 
stimulators-Clinical applications-Brain control and sensing of artificial 
limbs-Stimulation of peripheral nerve interfaces-Construction of implant-
wireless communication-prosthetic master control unit. 
4 
Fundamentals of Tissue Engineering: Engineering biomaterials for tissue 
engineering- Nano biomaterials for tissue engineering – Drug delivery & 
Gene therapy mechanism- Vascularization of Engineered Tissues-Tissue 
micro environments (Basic level of tissue engineering of nervous system, 
liver, kidney & cartilage). Fundamentals of 3 D printing and its applications 
in Biomedical engineering: Concept of 3D printing -3D printing process- 
Materials for 3D printing - Biomedical applications of 3 D printing 
technology- maxillofacial surgery & upper limb prosthetics. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
BIOMEDICAL SIGNAL PROCESSING & APPLICATIONS  
Course Code 
PEEBT634 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBEBT504 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To familiarize with concepts of advanced digital signal processing techniques which includes 
adaptive filtering, wavelet analysis, power spectrum, estimation and multivariate analysis 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Power spectrum analysis: Estimation of power density spectrum, non-
parametric methods- Periodogram - Bartlett, Welch, Blackman and Tukey 
Methods-comparison. Parametric models, estimation Auto regressive (AR), 
Moving average (MA) Autoregressive moving average (ARMA) models. 
Parametric model based linear prediction theory-Forward and backward 
linear prediction Estimation of parameters - spectrum estimation of ECG, 
Power spectrum estimation of Heart rate variability data. Application, 
Spectrum estimation of EEG 
9 
2 
Wavelet Analysis Introduction to wavelet transforms – CWT & DWT 
Orthogonal wavelet decomposition, Orthonormal wavelets - filter banks. 
Applications of DWT: wavelet denoising, ECG feature detection & Heart 
sound Analysis. 
9 
3 
Adaptive filters: Optimal and adaptive filters, Weiner filters, Adaptive signal 
processing - Steepest descent algorithm LMS adaptive algorithm, Adaptive 
noise canceller – cancellation of 50 Hz signal in ECG- cancellation of 
maternal ECG in foetal electrocardiography 
9 

 
 
4 
Multivariate Analysis: Principal Component Analysis – denoising of ECG & 
EEG signals using PCA, Independent Component Analysis-EEG denoising. 
Computation of diagnostic signal parameters of ECG: Heart rate and QRS 
detection using Multivariate analysis (PCA and ICA). 
9

SEMESTER S6 
COMPUTATIONAL METHODS IN BIOMEDICAL ENGINEERING  
Course Code 
PEEBT636 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Introduce practical computational methods for data analysis, modelling and simulation of 
biomedical engineering. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to Computational Methods: Overview of computational 
methods 
in 
biomedical 
engineering, 
Basic 
programming 
skills 
(Python/MATLAB) Variables and operations, conditional statements (if, elif, 
else) and  loops (for, while), Defining and calling functions, Data Structures, 
File handling, Libraries for Numerical Computing and Data analysis, Data 
Visualization 
9 
2 
Numerical Methods for Solving Equations: Root finding methods (bisection, 
Newton-Raphson) Solving linear and nonlinear equations Applications in 
biomedical engineering. 
9 
3 
Introduction to modeling and simulation: Ordinary differential equations 
(ODEs) and their applications, Modeling of biological processes (neuronal 
dynamics, cell electrophysiology) Partial Differential Equations (PDEs): 
Describing spatial and temporal variations in phenomena such as heat 
transfer in tissues and fluid flow in blood vessels. 
9 
4 
Bioinformatics: Sequence Analysis: Algorithms for DNA, RNA, and protein 
sequence alignment. Structural Bioinformatics: Molecular modeling and 
simulation techniques for studying protein structures and interactions. 
Genomics and Proteomics: Computational tools for analyzing genomic and 
proteomic data to understand gene expression and protein functions. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
MEDICAL ROBOTICS 
Course Code 
PEEBT635 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBEBT504 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Gain comprehensive knowledge of the basic principles of robotics, including core components such as 
sensors, actuators, and drive mechanisms.  
2. Examine the kinematics and dynamics of robotic systems, focusing on their practical applications in 
healthcare also develop and implement programs for controlling robots to improve medical procedures 
and patient care. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Components of robotic system: History of medical robots, Classification of 
medical robots, Present status and future trends. Basic components of robotic 
system. Basic terminology- Accuracy, Repeatability, Resolution, Degree of 
freedom. Mechanisms and transmission, End effectors, Grippers different 
methods of gripping, Mechanical grippers-Slider crank mechanism, Screw 
type, Rotary actuators, Cam type gripper, Magnetic grippers, Vacuum 
grippers, Air operated grippers; Specifications of robot. 
9 
2 
Drive systems and Sensors Drive system- Pneumatic Drives-Hydraulic 
Drives-Mechanical Drives, Electrical Drives-D.C. Servo Motors, Stepper 
Motors, A.C. Servo Motors-Salient Features, Applications and Comparison. 
Sensors in robots – Touch sensors, Tactile sensor, Proximity and range 
sensors, Robotic vision sensor, Force sensor, Light sensors, Pressure sensors 
9 
3 
Robot kinematics and robot programming Forward Kinematics, Inverse 
Kinematics and Difference; Forward Kinematics and Reverse Kinematics of 
9 

 
 
manipulators with Two, Three Degrees of Freedom (in 2 Dimension), Four 
Degrees of freedom (in 3 Dimension) Jacobians, Velocity and Forces 
Manipulator Dynamics, Trajectory Generator, Manipulator Mechanism 
Design-Derivations and problems. Lead through Programming, Robot 
programming Languages-VAL Programming 
4 
Robots in healthcare: Tele operated Robot-Assisted Minimally Invasive 
Surgery, Robot design concepts Robot assisted Image-Guided Interventions: 
CT, MR, Ultrasound, Other applications: Robotic catheters for heart 
electrophysiology, Humanoids, Micro/Nano robots for biomedicine - 
Delivery, 
surgery, 
sensing, 
and 
detoxification. 
Case 
Studies: 
Characterization of gestures to the design of robots- Design methodologies- 
Technological choices - Security. Cardiac, abdominal, and urologic 
procedures with tele-operated robots (3 procedures each), Neurosurgery and 
Orthopaedic surgery with robots.  
9

SEMESTER S6 
MEDICAL IMAGE PROCESSING 
Course Code 
PBEBT604 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide an overview of the nature of human visual perception, the elements of an 
image-processing system which includes sampling, quantisation and two dimensional 
transforms. 
2. To make the students familiar with image enhancement, restoration, segmentation, 
classification, machine learning and deep learning techniques for image analysis. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Image perception -MTF of the visual system –monochrome vision models - 
color vision model. Image sampling and quantization: Two-dimensional 
sampling theory, Image quantization - uniform quantizer. Image transforms -
Two dimensional orthogonal and unitary transforms - properties of unitary 
transforms, 2D DFT, DCT, Hadamard, Haar, KL transforms. 
9 
2 
Image enhancement: contrast enhancement, clipping and thresholding - 
digital negative, intensity level slicing - bit extraction. Histogram processing, 
Magnification and interpolation. Image Enhancement in Spatial domain: 
Smoothing and sharpening operations in time domain, Filtering in frequency 
domain: Smoothing and sharpening frequency domain filters, Homomorphic 
filtering. 
9 
3 
Image restoration: Image degradation, Noise, Blurring, Modelling image 
degradation, Inverse filtering, Wiener filtering. Image segmentation- 
Thresholding- optimal, adaptive, Region-based methods- region growing and 
9 

 
 
region merging, Boundary-based methods- edge detection and linking, 
boundary tracking. 
4 
Feature recognition and classification: Features - describing the contents 
and the shape of objects. Classification- Supervised and unsupervised 
learning. Discriminant analysis, k-nearest-Neighbor (kNN) classifier. 
Unsupervised- k-means clustering. Deep Learning for Medical Image 
Analysis, Convolutional Neural Networks. Image fusion for hybrid imaging, 
Super resolution imaging. 
9 
 
Suggestion on Project Implementation 
● In the first class, students shall be given an awareness and/ or guidelines on how to implement 
and learn this course through a project and are asked to form groups of maximum five 
members in the first week. 
● Each group should identify a project where different image processing techniques can be used 
for biomedical image processing applications and perform a literature survey. 
● Choose a suitable dataset, proper processing techniques and suitable machine learning, deep 
learning or computer vision algorithms for your application. 
● Develop the block diagram, the algorithms, the flowchart and necessary codes and present 
them before the jury within the first month after the commencement of classes. 
● Implement the necessary algorithms. 
● Prepare a report and present before the jury for final evaluation. 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 60 marks, ESE: 40 marks)

SEMESTER S6 
BIOSENSORS & TRANSDUCERS 
Course Code 
OEEBT611 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Learn the basic principles of biosensors, transducers & their applications. 
2. Provide students an insight into biopotentials and electrodes. 
3. Introduce Nano biosensors & their applications.  
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
TRANSDUCERS: 
Classification 
of 
transducers, 
characteristic 
of 
transducers. Temperature transducers: Resistance temperature detector 
(RTD), Thermistor, Thermocouple, chemical thermometry. Displacement 
transducers: potentiometer, resistive strain gauges, inductive displacement, 
capacitive 
displacement 
transducer. 
Pressure 
transducer: 
variable 
capacitance pressure transducers, LVDT transducers, strain gauge 
transducers, catheter tip transducers, Piezoelectric transducer.  Photoelectric 
transducers: photo-emissive tubes, photovoltaic cell, photoconductive cell, 
photodiodes. 
9 
2 
BIO-POTENTIAL ELECTRODES: Electrode theory, Skin Contact 
Impedance. Types of Electrodes: Microelectrodes-Metal microelectrodes, 
micropipette (metal filled glass and glass micropipette electrodes). Depth 
and needle electrodes- Depth electrode, Needle electrode. Surface 
electrodes- Metal plate surface electrodes, Suction Cup electrode, Adhesive 
tape electrode, Multipoint electrode. BIO-POTENTIALS: ECG - 
9 

 
 
Generation of cardiac action potentials- Characteristics of ECG Signal, 
Einthoven’s triangle -Lead Systems.  Electrodes for ECG acquisition. EEG – 
Electroencephalogram - Brain action potentials - Characteristics of signal-
Electrodes and 10-20 system for EEG signal acquisition. Evoked Potentials. 
EMG - Electrical activity of muscles – Characteristics of EMG signal. 
Electrodes for EMG acquisition. (Instrumentation not needed for ECG, EEG 
& EMG) 
3 
FUNDAMENTALS OF BIOSENSORS-Basic Principle, Characteristics of 
a Biosensor. Types - Based on Transducer: Electrochemical- Amperometric, 
Potentiometric; optical-Surface plasmon resonance, Evanescent Wave 
Fluorescence Biosensors; piezo electric; calorimetric biosensors. Based on 
Bio 
recognition 
elements 
in 
biosensors- 
natural-semisynthetic-
synthetic.Immobilization methods  ISFET, Enzyme electrodes. Principles of 
Fiber-Optic Sensing- Definitions, Classification, Working Principles. 
Applications of Biosensors-Biosensors for clinical diagnostics-Glucose 
detection- cancer detection. 
9 
4 
NANO BIOSENSORS: Significance, Types of Nanomaterials- Gold 
Nano-particles, Quantum Dots, Carbon Nanotubes & Graphene (Key 
features). Synthesis of Nanomaterials-Top-down Approach & Bottom down 
Approach. 
Types 
of 
nano 
biosensors: 
nanotubes-based 
sensors, 
nanoparticles-based biosensors, nanowire-based sensors, quantum dots-based 
sensors (Basics of sensing only). Application of Nanomaterial based 
biosensors: Metal nanoparticle-based biosensors, carbon nanotube-based 
biosensors. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
BIOMECHANICS   
 
Course Code 
OEEBT612 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L:3 T: P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NONE 
Course Type 
OE 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course enables students to understand the biomechanics of human tissues and apply the 
engineering knowledge for design of prosthetic devices and implants 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Biomechanics of Hard Tissues -   structure and mechanical properties of 
bone - cortical and cancellous bones, Elasticity-stress, strain, elastic 
modulus, Poisson’s ratio, yield strength, ultimate tensile strength, failure 
strength, strain to failure, Wolff’s law of bone remodeling, models of 
viscoelasticity - Soft Tissues - Structure, functions, material properties – 
tendon function, elasticity in a tendon-mechanical properties 
9 
2 
Joint prosthesis-components-materials- shoulder, Hip, Knee-Human gait-
phases-gait analysis methods-sensors- postural stability-gait analysis-human 
gait in health and disease. 
9 
3 
 Fracture fixation devices-pins, screws, intramedullary devices, plates-
materials for fracture fixators-Dental implants-types-materials-heart valves-
types – mechanical and tissue heart valves-materials-testing of heart valves 
9 
4 
 Basics of 3D printing technology- Bioinks for 3D printing of artificial 
extracellular matrices-Printing technologies used in three dimensional

SEMESTER S6 
BIOSIGNALS & SIGNAL PROCESSING 
 
Course Code 
OEEBT613 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the structure and function of excitable cells, explore the ionic basis of cardiac 
action potentials and the specialized conductive system of the heart. 
2. Learn to generate, interpret, and analyze ECG waveforms, as well as understand EEG brain 
rhythms, signal characteristics, and electrode systems. Study EMG signals, along with the 
characteristics of heart sounds. 
3. Identify and mitigate various types of noise in biopotential recordings using time domain 
filters and frequency domain filters. Perform power spectrum analysis and conduct spectrum 
analysis of bio signals.  
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Cell Potentials: Excitable cells - cell membrane - structure. Nernst potential- 
Resting membrane potential - Goldman Hodgkin Katz equation. Specialized 
excitatory and conductive system of heart - rhythmicity- ionic basis of 
cardiac action potentials – plateau region – pacemaker. Nerve action 
potentials – ionic basis of generation, properties and refractory period. 
Synapse  -Neurotransmitters – types 
9 
2 
ECG: Generation – ECG – waves – duration – intervals – segments - Lead 
systems-unipolar & bipolar. EEG - Brain rhythms &waves - characteristics 
of signal - Electrode system. EMG: Membrane potentials & Action 
potentials in smooth muscles –Characteristics of EMG signal. Heart sounds – 
9 

 
 
Phonocardiography. PPG – characteristics - dicrotic notch. Introduction to 
other biopotentials – ENG& EGG (Instrumentation not needed for ECG, 
EEG & EMG) 
3 
Event detection in ECG - QRS detection -Derivative based method-Pan 
Tompkins algorithm. Detection of P Wave. Dicrotic notch detection. EEG 
rhythm detection -Correlation based method. Detection of S1 &S2 heart 
sound. EMG envelop extraction 
Noise: Random Noise -structured noise-physiologic interference, Time 
domain filters: synchronised averaging- moving averaging-derivative based 
operators. Noise removal in ECG: random noise removal -baseline drift 
removal. Frequency domain filters: Butterworth low pass &low filter. 
Adaptive filters – cancellation of 50 Hz signal in ECG 
9 
4 
Power spectrum analysis: Estimation of power density spectrum, non-
parametric method-Periodogram &modified periodogram. Parametric 
methods -ARMA model-based PSD estimation. Spectrum analysis of bio 
signals- spectrum estimation of ECG-Power spectrum estimation of Heart 
rate variability data. Spectrum estimation of EEG 
9

SEMESTER S6 
BIOMATERIALS  
Course Code 
OEEBT614 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min.  
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Study the classification, bonding, crystal structure, mechanical behaviour, and applications of 
metals, polymers, and ceramics in medical implants. 
2. Explore the structure, properties, and applications of collagen-based biomaterials in tissue 
engineering, focusing on mechanical behaviour and tissue regeneration. 
3. Evaluate the factors influencing biocompatibility and blood compatibility of implant 
materials, and apply appropriate testing methods for their design and selection. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Metals for implants- Classification – Metals-Stainless steel-Co-Cr alloys-Ti 
based alloys-Bonding and crystal structure-interstitial sites-crystallographic 
planes and directions-theoretical shear strength Imperfections in metals and 
alloys-defects-metal processing for improved material properties-corrosion 
processes-Applications of metals in medical implants. Composites-
Structure–properties-anisotropy particulate composites-fibrous composites-
porous materials-biocompatibility of composites sterilization, and materials 
selection for implant design-Successful device performance and implant 
design. 
9  
2 
Polymers-Bonding and crystal structure-Molecular weight distribution in 
polymers- Structure-Polymers used as biomaterials-sterilization-surface 
9  

 
 
modification to improve biocompatibility-chemo gradient surfaces for cell 
and protein integration- Mechanical behaviour of polymers Polymer 
processing Polymers in medical implants- Ceramic materials- Bonding and 
crystal structure-Mechanical behaviour of ceramics-Fracture behaviour and 
toughening mechanisms-thermal stresses-processing of ceramics ceramics in 
medical implants 
3 
Tissue derived biomaterials-Structure and Properties of Collagen and 
Collagen-Rich Tissues Biotechnology of Collagen-Design of a Restorable 
Collagen-Based Medical Implant-Tissue Engineering for Tissue and Organ 
Regeneration. Mechanical behaviour of structural tissues microstructure and 
mechanical properties of the basic building blocks of structural tissues-
hierarchical organization of dental tissues, bone, tendons, ligaments, 
cartilage, skin, and blood vessels-macroscopic mechanical performance of 
tissues based on their microstructure -compare and contrast the mechanical 
performance of various structural tissues 
9  
4 
Biocompatibility – Definition. Factors affecting biocompatibility – 
Carcinogenicity, mutagenecity, cytogenicity, toxicity. Blood Compatibility – 
Factors affecting blood compatibility. Material response: Swelling and 
leaching, Corrosion and Dissolution, Reaction of Biological molecules with 
biomaterial surfaces. Testing of implants: Methods of test for biological 
performance- In vitro and In vivo implant test methods. Clinical testing of 
implant Materials, Design and selection of implant materials – Design 
Process. 
9

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
● Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test understanding 
of the upcoming experiment. 
● Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of the 
theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
● Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
● Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
● Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
● Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper documentation 
of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
● Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
● Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles during 
a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, 
and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
 
 

 
 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
● Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
● Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
● Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
● Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
● Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or programming 
task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
● Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
● Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality of 
program output. 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
● Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
● Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the subject. 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
● Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER S7 
POWER ELECTRONICS & APPLICATIONS  
 
Course Code 
PEEBT741 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Introduce various power electronic devices 
2. Design & analyze power conversion circuits having applications in Biomedical field 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Power electronic devices: Power diodes, Power transistors, MOSFETS and 
IGBTs. 
Structure, 
fabrication, 
Regions 
of 
operations, 
Switching 
characteristics- turn ON and turn OFF switching waveforms, Safe operating 
area, Paralleling of transistors. Thyristor family: SCRs, DIAC, TRIAC and 
GTOs. V I characteristics of SCR.  
Introduction to classification of power electronic circuits: AC-DC 
converters, DC-DC converters, DC-AC converters and AC-AC converters. 
Application of power devices in renewable energy systems and Electric 
vehicles. 
9 
2 
AC-DC converters: Single phase-controlled rectifiers – half wave, full-wave, 
half-controlled and fully controlled. typical waveforms with R, RL, RL with 
diode and RL with voltage source - voltage and current equation for half-
wave-controlled rectifier. Three phase half-wave and full-wave controlled 
rectifier with R load, waveforms. 
9 

 
 
3 
DC-DC converters: Basic chopper operation using semiconductor switches, 
Buck, Boost and Buck-Boost converters, Selection of devices, Electrical and 
thermal stress, Isolated converters, Half bridge and full bridge converters, 
Understanding governing equations and switching waveforms. DC-AC 
Inverters, Square wave operations, half bridge and full bridge inverters. 
9 
4 
Carrier based unipolar and bipolar PWM inverters, Effect of harmonics and 
its elimination, Sinusoidal PWM inverters. Power electronic systems: Solar 
power plants, ON grid and OFF grid types, Traction control in EVs, Forward 
motoring and generating modes, PWM control techniques: voltage mode, 
current mode and gated oscillator controls, Closed loop responses and 
stabilization. Gate driver circuits, Isolated and non-isolated, types. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
HUMAN FACTORS IN ENGINEERING AND DESIGN  
 
Course Code 
PEEBT742 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the basic concepts and techniques employed in broad area of  human factors 
engineering focusing on anthropometric principles in design of work places  and  to optimize 
the interaction between human and systems. 
2. Integrate human factor considerations in the design of medical devices and health care tools 
for improved user experience and safety. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Human factors Engineering – Definition, Human Factors 
& Systems - Aspects of Human-machine systems.  A model of Human 
information 
processing. 
Process 
of 
seeing- 
Visual 
capabilities- 
Accommodation, Visual acuity and Contrast sensitivity. Factors affecting 
visual capabilities. Human factor aspects of hard copy text and computer 
screen text. Graphic representations of Text & Data. Human factors in 
designing Symbols & Codes 
    9 
2 
Visual Displays - Qualitative visual displays, Quantitative visual displays, 
Signals & Warning lights, Representational Displays-Aircraft Bank Angle 
displays-Principles of aircraft position displays.  Auditory Displays - 
Process of hearing. Principles of auditory displays, Auditory Displays for 
Specific Purposes. Cutaneous Senses- Tactual Displays-, Substitute for 
Hearing, seeing, Tactual graph. Compatibility – Types of Compatibility-
Conceptual, movement, spatial and Modality Compatibility. Movement 
compatibility- Rotary controls and rotary displays in same plane and 
      9 

 
 
different plane.  
       3 
Muscle Physiology- Work Physiology. Measure of physiological strain, 
Physical Workload, Strength & Endurance. Manual Material Handling 
(MMH), Bio-mechanical recommended limits of MMH. Reducing the risk of 
MMH overexertion. General principles of Biomechanical Design. 
Anthropometry -Anthropometric design principles. Static and Dynamic 
Anthropometry. Case study of Anthropometric Design- Viewing Angle 
determination of Cardiac Output Monitor. Work place and Seating Design-
Work space envelope, Factors in design of workspace surfaces, Principles of 
seat design. 
     9 
4 
 Classification of human errors-Dealing with human errors. Accidents - 
Theories of accident causation-CFAC model. Occupational Safety and 
Health - Industrial Safety and Health, Hazards and Control Measures, 
Warnings and Safety Programs. Human factors for Mobile medical device 
design - General and special considerations, Design principles for home 
healthcare; Consideration related to Hand tool design in health care. Case 
studies exemplifying design for device mobility and use in motion: Infusion 
pumps, Portable X-Ray machine, Portable Ultrasound Device, Transport 
ventilator. 
      9

SEMESTER S7 
FUNDAMENTALS OF BIOMEMS AND MICROFLUIDICS 
 
Course Code 
PEEBT743 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Student will get the fundamental understanding of BioMEMS, micro-systems and a 
variety of diagnostic and therapeutic applications including intelligent biochips and 
sensors. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
MEMS 
Material 
and 
Fabrication: 
Typical 
MEMs 
and 
Microsystems,Compare MEMS and BioMEMS, materials for MEMS -
Silicon and its compounds, Silicon piezo resistors, Gallium Arsenide, 
quartz, polymers. Micromachining techniques-photolithography, thin film 
deposition, doping-diffusion, ion implantation, etching, Bulk machining, 
LIGA process, wafer bonding. 
9 
2 
Sensors And Actuators: Mechanical sensors and actuators – beam and 
cantilever –microplates, strain, pressure and flow measurements. Thermal 
sensors and actuators-actuator based on thermal expansion, thermo 
couples, thermal resistor. Electrostatic sensors and actuators- Parallel 
plate capacitor, pull in effect,Inertia sensor. Piezoelectric sensor and 
actuator: Properties of piezoelectric materials, – inchworm motor, Pressure 
sensor. 
9 
3 
Microfluidic Systems: Fluid dynamics, continuity equation, momentum 
equation, equation of motion, laminar flow in circular conduits, fluid flow 
in micro conduits, fluid actuation methods. Dielectrophoresis, microfluid 
dispenser, microneedle, micro pumps, micro valves.  
9 

 
 
4 
Application of BioMEMS: CAD for MEMS, micro total analysis systems 
(MicroTAS)-Lab-on-a-Chip- detection and measurement, microsystem 
approaches to polymerase chain reaction (PCR). MEMS based drug 
delivery-Drug delivery to the brain, Ocular drug delivery, Gastrointestinal 
tract drug delivery – capsule endoscopy, Transdermal drug delivery, 
Implantable subcutaneous drug delivery. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
ASSISTIVE MEDICAL DEVICES  
 
Course Code 
PEEBT744 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the basic concepts of technology behind assistive devices for persons with 
different kinds of disabilities 
2. Introduce the different types of assistive technologies currently available to provide a better 
quality of life  
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Definitions and Principles of Assistive Technology, The 
HAAT Model - Applications, Universal and Specialized designs, Modified 
or Adapted Commercial Technology. A Functional Framework for 
Assistive Technologies: Allocation of functions, Hard and Soft assistive 
technologies, Application of ethical concepts in assistive technology. 
Human/ Technology Interfaces: Anatomic Sites for Control of AT, 
Elements of the Human/Technology Interface. 
9 
2 
Control Interfaces for AT: Characteristics, Control interfaces for Direct 
and– Keyboards- types, Enhancing keyboard control, Touch screens, 
Electronic Pointing interfaces, Joysticks, Eye-Gaze systems, BCI, Control 
interfaces for indirect selection - Switches, Switch arrays, Discrete Joysticks, 
and 
Chord 
Keyboards. 
Multiple 
versus 
Integrated 
CI. 
Assistive 
Technologies for Seating and Positioning: Biomechanical principles, 
Sitting posture and center of pressure, Seating technologies. Wheeled 
Mobility: Supporting structure, Frame types, Propelling structure, 
9 

 
 
Specialized bases, Smart Wheelchairs, Factors considered for selecting a 
wheelchair, Safe transportation of individuals in wheelchairs. 
3 
Assistive Technologies for manipulation: Low-technology Aids for 
manipulation, Special-purpose electromechanical aids for manipulation, 
Electronic aids to daily living, Robotic aids - Principles of Assistive Robots, 
Robots as personal assistants, Mobile assistive robots, Robot use by children. 
Assistive Technologies for Vision: Reading aids, Optical and non-optical 
aids, Electronic aids, Braille displays, Recorded audio materials, Automatic 
reading of text, Mobility and orientation Aids – Canes, Alternative mobility 
devices, Electronic Travel Aids for Obstacle Detection, Orientation, and 
Mobility – Electronically augmented canes, Head-mounted glasses, 
Navigation aids for the blind – GPS-based, Special purpose visual aids.  
9 
4 
Assistive Technologies for hearing impaired and deaf: Hearing aids – 
Types – Body worn, Behind the ear, Spectacles aid, In the ear, Bone 
conduction, Middle ear implant, Cochlear implant, Auditory brain stem 
implant aids, Audio frequency induction loop systems, IR systems, Alarm 
and alerting devices – audio, visual and tactile alarms, Devices for deafblind 
– Braille devices, fingerprinting. Assistive Technologies for Cognitive 
Augmentation: Cognitive disorders – Congenital – Intellectual, learning, 
ADHD, Autism, Acquired disorders – Dementia, Brain injury, Stroke, 
Cognitive Assistive Technologies – Devices to aid memory, Time 
management, Prompting/Cueing/Coaching Devices. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
DEEP LEARNING TECHNIQUES 
 
Course Code 
PEEBT746 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic concepts of 
neural networks.
Course Type 
PE 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understanding Deep Learning Architectures: Learn about popular deep learning architectures 
such as AlexNet, VGG16, GoogLeNet, ResNet, and DenseNet. Understand their design 
principles, layer types, and applications. 
2. Hands-on Experience with Deep Learning Platforms: Gain practical experience with deep 
learning platforms like Keras, TensorFlow, and PyTorch. Explore data types, tensor 
operations, model configuration, training, and testing. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Convolutional Neural Network (CNN), Convolution layer, Activation 
function, Pooling Layer, Dense Layer, Transfer learning, Deep CNN 
architectures. Feedforward Neural Networks, Backpropagation, Gradient 
Descent, Loss functions, Optimizers, Train/Val/Test dataset distributions, 
Performance matrix. Hyper parameter tuning, Bias Variance trade-off, 
Problem of overfitting, Regularization, Batch normalization, Dataset 
augmentation. Applications 
9 
2 
Deep learning Networks: History-AlexNet, GoogLeNet, VGGNet, ResNet, 
Dense Net Deep learning platforms: Keras, Theano, TensorFlow and 
PyTorch. Tensor Flow: data Types, Tensors, create Tensors, operations on 
Tensors, Tensor Board Keras: Common Functional Modules, Model 
Configuration, Training, and Testing. 
9 

 
 
3 
Recurrent Neural Networks Forwards and Backward pass. Gradient 
propagation. Backpropagation through time (BPTT) algorithm. Many-to-one 
RNN model (sentiment analysis), Many-to-many RNN model (language 
model), Vanishing gradients in Recurrent networks LSTMs, Bidirectional 
RNNs, Gated RNNs, Encoder-Decoder Models, Attention Networks Issues 
in RNN/LSTM. 
9 
4 
Deep 
Autoencoders: 
Unsupervised 
Deep 
Learning, 
Autoencoders 
Undercomplete autoencoders, Regularized autoencoders - Applications 
Generative Modelling: Variational Autoencoder (VAE). Variational 
Learning, VAE: network architecture. Generative Adversarial networks 
(GANs), Boltzmann Machines, Restricted Boltzmann Machines. Deep 
reinforcement learning: Reinforcement learning RL Process Reward 
hypothesis, Observations/States Space Action Space Rewards. The Policy π: 
the agent’s brain Policy-Based Methods, Value based methods. Deep 
reinforcement learning-Q-learning, actor-critic, policy gradient, experience 
replay. Applications. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
ADVANCED MEDICAL IMAGING & IMAGE PROCESSING 
TECHNIQUES 
Course Code 
PEEBT745 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. The students will be introduced to the advanced image processing techniques for medical 
images as well as texture based analysis method for biomedical applications. 
2. The students will be able to understand active shape models used for medical image data and 
the image archival systems. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Multi-modal images and Hybrid Imaging: Hybrid PET/CT Systems, 
PET/MRI Systems. Super resolution imaging. Image Fusion: Preprocessing 
measures-geometrical transformations and image interpolation, Distortion 
identification- disparity analysis. Image Registration- Global Similarity, 
Transform Identification, Registration Evaluation and Approval. Three-
Dimensional Data from Two-Dimensional Slices, Panorama Fusion, Stereo 
Surface Reconstruction.  
9 
2 
Texture in Biomedical Images: Image intensity versus image texture, 
Characterizing the Texture, From Markov Random Fields to Fractals, From 
Markov Random Fields to Gibbs Distributions, Local binary patterns 
(LBPs),  Co-occurrence Matrices, Generalized Co-occurrence Matrices, 
Orientation Histograms, Textons, From Spatio-Frequency to Spatio-
Structural Space, Statistical Spatio-Structural Space, Monogenic Signal, 
From Monogenic Signal Back to Gabor Functions. Deep Learning 
Techniques on Texture Analysis- Lung nodule detection in CT scans. 
9 
3 
Active Shape and Active Appearance Models: Creating an ASM, Using 
ASMs for Segmentation, The Active Appearance Model, Deficiencies of 
9 

 
 
Statistical Shape Models, Changing the Parametric Model, Using a Part-
Based Model, Using a Non-parametric Model, Physically-Based Shape 
Models, Mass-Spring Models, Finite Element Models, Shape, Appearance 
and Pose Priors for Segmentation, Atlas-Based Segmentation, Combining 
Shape Information with Level Set Segmentation,  Solutions Based on Graph 
Cuts, Graph Cuts on Pre-segmented Images 
4 
Image Storage and Transfer: Image Management: Archiving- Image 
Storage and Transfer, Information Systems in a Hospital, The DICOM 
Standard, Establishing DICOM Connectivity, The DICOM File Format, 
Technical Properties of Medical Images, Displays and Workstations, HL7 
standard, 
Principles 
of 
Image 
Compression 
for 
Archiving 
and 
Communication- Philosophy of Image Compression, Generic Still-Image 
Compression. System, Principles of Lossless Compression, Predictive 
Coding, Principles of Lossy Compression, Pixel-Oriented Methods, Block-
Oriented Methods, Global Compression Methods. 
9

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

Criteria for Evaluation(Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 5 points) 
a) Clearly defines the problem. 
b) Examines and identifies the relevant factors. 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 5 points) 
a) Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 5 points) 
a) Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
4. Conclusion (K3- 3 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a) Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, and depth of understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S7 
COMMUNICATION TECHNIQUES 
Course Code 
PEEBT751 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1.   Develop a comprehensive understanding of both analog and digital communication systems, 
including fundamental principles, modulation techniques, and key components of advanced 
communication systems like microwave, satellite, and optical communications. 
2.   Gain proficiency in digital modulation schemes, understand the evolution of mobile 
communication technologies from 1G to 5G, and learn about modern wireless 
communication systems and multiple access techniques. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to communication systems: Definition, Block level 
representation. Analog and digital communication systems: Comparison, 
Need for modulation Amplitude Modulation: Representation of AM, 
Modulation index, Frequency spectrum, Power relations in AM wave, AM 
Generation, Envelope AM Detection, Superheterodyne AM receiver, 
Balanced modulator Frequency modulation: Mathematical representation, 
waveforms, frequency deviation, bandwidth requirement, FM Generation– 
Varactor Diode Modulator & Armstrong method, Pre-emphasis and De-
emphasis, Balanced slope detector, FM transmitters and FM receivers (block 
diagram) 
9 
2 
 Pulse Modulation: Need for pulse modulation, Different types, Pulse 
Amplitude Modulation, Pulse Width Modulation, Pulse Position Modulation 
and Pulse Code Modulation – principles of operation. Digital Modulation 
Schemes: BPSK, QPSK, BFSK, Differential Phase Shift Keying (DPSK), 
QAM. Modems: Classification, Modes of operation, Modem interfacing 
9 
3 
Microwave communication system: Introduction- transmitter- repeater- 
9 

 
 
receiver, frequency bands. Satellite communication system: Introduction- 
transponder, Kepler’s laws, Satellite sub systems. Optical communication 
system: Features: fiber optic technology- total internal reflection- Snell’s 
law- light transmission through an optical fiber- numerical aperture, Optical 
fiber communication system. Cellular communications: Principles of 
cellular networks, frequency reuse, operation of cellular system, hand off 
strategies, roaming, improving capacity in cellular system.  
4 
Wireless communication systems: Introduction to modern wireless 
communication systems, Wireless local area networks, Bluetooth and 
Personal Area networks. Introduction to Multiple Access: FDMA, TDMA, 
Spread Spectrum Multiple Access, Space division Multiple Access, CDMA, 
OFDM. GSM services, architecture of GSM network. Overview of Mobile 
Communication Generations (1G to 4G), Evolution and Need for 5G, 5G 
Network Architecture and Components 
9

Course Code

CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R)

None
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Student will be able to get an overview of design concepts for a medical device starting 
from generating ideas, classifying medical devices and understanding the design 
procedures. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Life cycle of Medical device; Determining and Documenting device 
requirements: Idea feasibility/Generating concept: Prototype development 
to prove the idea. Requirements: Product specification, Specification 
review, design specification Software/Hardware requirement specification, 
Software/Hardware design description, Device History Record, Device 
Master Record, Design history files. 
9  
2 
Design Phase – Risk analysis- hazards review, risk trace matrix, Risk 
assessment of Medical device-FMEA: Design and system FMEA, 
Hardware design, Software design, design reviews, environmental 
protection, product misuse, Biocompatibility – sterilization requirements 
(sterilization and packaging), human factors engineering, Bill of materials 
preparation, Need of CAD in product design. Application of AI tools in 
device designing. 
9 
3 
Verification and Validation: Validation and verification meaning and 
differences, Design verification plan, protocol, software-hardware test plan 
for medical devices, system testing- types of testing. Manufacturing supply 
chain: Product manufacturing, IQ/OQ/PQ, Design transfer process to 
9  

 
 
manufacturing, Labelling-IFU, Quality assurance, audits. 
4 
Fundamentals of Medical device regulation:  Medical device definition, 
classification (FDA, EU and CDSCO); Medical device safety, Global 
framework for regulations, Regulatory tools, Medical device Standards: 
Development 
process, 
Conformity 
assessment, 
Quality 
system 
requirements; Basic awareness on ISO 13485, 14971, 10993, 11607, 
62304, IEC 60601.  
9

SEMESTER S7 
NEURAL PROSTHESIS AND IMPLANTS 
Course Code 
PEEBT753 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Comprehend the various challenges involved in the design and implementation of upper limb 
prostheses, including anatomical, functional, and technical constraints. 
2. Investigate different types of upper limb prostheses and evaluate their effectiveness, 
considering the needs of diverse user groups and the limitations imposed by current 
technologies. 
3. Utilize knowledge of the human motor system and control strategies to innovate and improve 
the development of upper limb prosthetics, ensuring better integration with the user's natural 
movements and enhancing overall usability. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Microelectronic Visual Prostheses: Microelectronic visual implant 
technologies: Retinal stimulation and retinal implant - Epiretinal, Subretinal 
and Extraocular implants, Visual stimulation in the brain, Optic Nerve 
Stimulation, Engineering challenges in the development of visual prostheses, 
Stimulation microelectrode arrays - types and electrode materials, optic 
nerve stimulation using penetrating microelectrode arrays, Neural electrical 
stimulator, DSP-based image processing system for visual prostheses 
9 
2 
Modern Cochlear Implant: System Review - Architecture and functional 
block diagram of a modern cochlear implants, External unit, RF link, Internal 
unit, Electrodes, Safety Considerations, Auditory Prosthesis Using Deep 
Brain Stimulation: Development and Implementation-Design considerations, 
approaches for implementation, Electrode technologies, Stimulation 
Strategies.  
9 

 
 
3 
Signals and Signal Processing for Myoelectric Control:  Myoelectric 
Signal - Acquisition, Processing, Control of prosthetic function, Terminal 
device electronics 
9 
4 
Upper Limb Prosthetics: Pre-prosthetic Assessment, Prosthetic Options, 
Components for the Upper Limb Prosthesis - Hands and Work Hands 
(Terminal Devices), Pinch Force, Weight, Work Hands, Cosmetic/Protective 
Covers, Electric wrist rotation, Wrist Flexion, Electronic Controllers, 
proportional Versus Digital control, Elbow components, All electric 
alternatives 
control 
Systems, 
Interface 
designs, 
Indications 
and 
contraindications, Training and outcome measurement  
9
