SEMESTER S7 
TISSUE ENGINEERING & BIOFABRICATION TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
 PEEBT754 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course aims to introduce students to the foundational concepts and technologies of 
biofabrication, including the principles of tissue engineering, biomaterials, and various 
fabrication techniques. Students will develop a deep understanding of scaffold design, 
cell culture methods, and advanced biofabrication technologies, preparing them to 
innovate in the field of regenerative medicine.  
2. This course focuses on the practical applications of tissue engineering in developing 
advanced tissue substitutes and regenerative solutions. Students will explore specific 
applications such as skin, bone, and cartilage engineering, and learn to utilize cutting-
edge technologies including 3D bioprinting and nanocomposite scaffolds, equipping them 
with skills to tackle real-world challenges in tissue engineering. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamental Of Tissue Engineering: Fundamentals Of Stem Cell Tissue 
Engineering; Growth Factors; Extracellular Matrix: Structure, Function And 
Tissue Engineering Application; Mechanical Forces On Cells; Cell 
Adhesion; Cell Migration. Tissue Engineering Enabling Technologies: 
Polymer Scaffold For Tissue Engineering Applications; Biomimetic 
Materials; Nanocomposite Scaffolds Tissue Engineering; Bioreactors; 
Regulatory Issues In Tissue Engineering. 
9 
2 
Tissue Engineering Application: Bioengineering Of Human Skin

produced ECM rich scaffold free constructs, the rotating wall vessel

of multicellular spheroids, Molding MCS, Bioprinting

SEMESTER S7 
ADVANCED COMPUTER PROGRAMMING TECHNIQUES 
 
Course Code 
PEEBT756

Teaching Hours/Week

Basic programming 
concepts.
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Implement R programs to extract data from different sources, as well as to clean 
and manipulate it. 
2. Develop advanced R programs for data analytics. 
3. Develop advanced Python programs for machine and deep learning. 
4. Analyse the ROS framework, architecture and interface. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Statistical programming language R: Downloading R and R Studio, Basics of 
Coding in R, Using Comments in R, Executing Commands in R, Importing 
Packages in R, Getting Data into R, Saving Output in R, Accessing Records 
and Variables in R, Slicing and Extracting Data, Variable Conversion, Data 
Selection and Manipulation, Math Function. Visualizations using the ggplot2 
library, Create commonly used data visualizations for each data type 
including histograms, scatter plots, and box plots, and improve data 
visualizations using facets. 
9 
2 
Advanced 
Data 
Processing-R 
programming-loading, 
manipulating, 
visualizing, and saving R Data Structures, sample-based statistics measuring 
central tendency and dispersion, different types of variables, scrapping data 
from public websites, examples of cohort-rebalancing. Statistical shape 
analysis using R, shape package, Shape distances in R, Tangent space 
coordinates in R, Calculation of mean shapes in R, Generalized Procrustes 
algorithms for shape analysis in R, tangent-based PCA. R packages for 
decision tree classification, random Forest R. R in Healthcare. 
9 

 
 
3 
Coding in python: Data analysis with pandas - the data structure of pandas,

algorithm, ANN for regression, Over fitting and cross fitting validation, 
regularization, convolutional neural networks, RNN, Tensor Flow and keras 
for deep convolutional neural networks. Deep neural network and transfer 
learning using Python, Tensorflow, and Keras. 
9

ROS Actuator Interfacing Case Studies: Navigation stack-creating 
transforms -odometer imu laser scan base controller robot configuration 
TurtleBot the low-cost mobile robot

SEMESTER S7 
ADVANCED BIOMEDICAL SIGNAL PROCESSING 
Course Code 
PEEBT755 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
NIL 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Students will learn various ECG data compression techniques, including direct data 
compression and transformation compression, as well as other techniques. They will also 
be able to apply ECG signal processing methods 
2. Students will gain knowledge about the fundamentals of speech signal processing and 
analyze speech signals through short-time speech analysis, frequency domain analysis, 
and understand key measures. 
3. Students will understand the modeling of EEG signals, and will learn methods for 
reducing artefacts in EEG signals. They will be able to conduct both parametric and non-
parametric spectral analysis, and perform EEG segmentation.  
4. For EMG signal processing, students will explore applications in various areas, as well as 
techniques for amplitude estimation, spectral analysis, and conduction velocity estimation 
of surface EMG signals. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
ECG Data Reduction: Direct data compression Techniques: Turning Point- 
AZTEC. Transformation Compression Techniques: Karhunen - Loeve 
Transform. Other data compression Techniques: Huffman coding 
ECG signal processing Techniques: Filtering: baseline removal by linear 
time variant filtering. Powerline interference removal by linear filter. Event 
detection: QRS detection basic steps – P Wave detection using time domain 
analysis. Morphological analysis of ECG- correlation coefficient -minimum 
9 

 
 
phase component. Heart rate variability analysis: time domain measures -
spectrum analysis of heart rate variability 
2 
Speech signal Processing Speech Fundamentals: Articulatory Phonetics – 
Production and Classification of Speech Sounds- Articulation- Voicing- 
Articulatory Model Speech Analysis: -short Time Speech Analysis - short 
time energy- short time average magnitude- short time zero crossing 
rateshort time ACF. Frequency domain analysis: Filter Banks- STFT- 
Spectrogram- Formant Estimation & analysis- Cepstral Analysis-MFCC 
9 
3 
Signal Processing Techniques in EEG Modelling the EEG signals: linear 
and stochastic EEG models -Time varying AR modelling. Artefacts in EEG: 
types – artefact reduction methods -linear filtering – Artifact cancellation 
using linearly combined reference signals -adaptive artefact cancellation. 
Non parametric spectral analysis-spectral parameters: Power in bands, 
spectral slope, peak frequency. Parametric spectrum estimation: Burg 
method. EEG segmentation-basics 
9 
4 
EMG Signal Processing Techniques EMG applications: Diagnostic EMG, 
Kinesiology, Ergonomics. Prosthesis control. Amplitude Estimation in the 
Surface EMG-Signal Model and ML Estimation, spectral analysis of surface 
EMG- Conduction velocity estimation -intramuscular EMG signal 
decomposition 
9

Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 5 points) 
a. Clearly defines the problem. 
b. Examines and identifies the relevant factors. 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 5 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 5 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
4. Conclusion (K3- 3 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate for the 
problem 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, and depth of understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S7 
BIOMEDICAL INSTRUMENTATION 
 
Course Code 
OEEBT721 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
OE/ ILE 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the principles of bioelectric potentials, including resting and action potentials, and 
their applications in clinical diagnostics such as ECG, EEG, and EMG. 
2. Learn the fundamentals of various biomedical imaging and measurement technologies, such 
as X-ray radiography, MRI, and ultrasound, and their applications in diagnosing and treating 
medical conditions. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Origin of bioelectric potentials – resting and action potentials - propagation 
of action potentials. Examples of bioelectric potentials - ECG, EEG, EMG, – 
Electrodes for measurement of biopotentials. Body surface electrodes, 
Microelectrodes, Transducers for measurement of temperature, pressure, 
displacement. Electrical activity of brain - Electro encephalogram – 10-20 
lead system, Instrumentation of EEG machine. Evoked potential -types & 
applications.  
9 
2 
Electrical activity of heart, electrocardiogram - lead systems -ECG machine 
– block diagram, Arrhythmia Monitor, Cardiac pacemakers – internal and 
external pacemakers, Defibrillators –principles of operation, Measurement of 
heart sounds –phonocardiography Measurement of blood pressure – 
sphygmomanometer & Oscillo metric methods. Photo plethysmography - for 
pulse rate measurement - Pulse oximeters, Patient monitoring systems. 
Heart-lung machine, Principle of operation, applications, Artificial heart 
valves. Electrical activity of Muscle – Electromyogram (EMG) –. 
9 

 
 
Electromyograph 
3 
Spirometer - measurement of respiratory parameters. Blood flow meters. 
Electromagnetic blood flow meter, Ultrasonic Doppler blood flow meter. 
Lithotripsy–principles, types- Ultrasonic lithotripsy, Extracorporeal shock 
wave lithotripsy (ESWL) &applications. Surgical diathermy – Principle of 
operation, applications, Ventilators- controls, modes, assisted mechanisms. 
9 
4 
X-ray radiography - Principles of x-ray generation – Block diagram of x-ray 
machine – X-ray computed tomography - Principle of operation, sectional 
imaging, scanner configurations. Ultrasonic imaging – Basic principles - 
Ultrasonic transducers- modes of image display-Principles & Applications. 
Magnetic resonance imaging -MRI instrumentation, Imaging modes. Electric 
shock hazards – Leakage currents – Test instruments for checking safety 
parameters of biomedical equipment. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
ASSISTIVE MEDICAL DEVICES  
Course Code 
OEEBT722 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To understand the basic concepts of technology behind assistive devices for persons with 
different kinds of disabilities 
2. Introduce the different types of assistive technologies currently available to provide a better 
quality of life  
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Definitions and Principles of Assistive Technology, The 
HAAT Model - Applications, Universal and Specialized designs, Modified 
or Adapted Commercial Technology. A Functional Framework for 
Assistive Technologies: Allocation of functions, Hard and Soft assistive 
technologies, Application of ethical concepts in assistive technology. 
Human/ Technology Interfaces: Anatomic Sites for Control of AT, 
Elements of the Human/Technology Interface. 
9 
2 
Control Interfaces for AT: Characteristics, Control interfaces for Direct 
and– Keyboards- types, Enhancing keyboard control, Touch screens, 
Electronic Pointing interfaces, Joysticks, Eye-Gaze systems, BCI, Control 
interfaces for indirect selection - Switches, Switch arrays, Discrete Joysticks, 
and 
Chord 
Keyboards. 
Multiple 
versus 
Integrated 
CI. 
Assistive 
Technologies for Seating and Positioning: Biomechanical principles, 
Sitting posture and center of pressure, Seating technologies. Wheeled 
Mobility: Supporting structure, Frame types, Propelling structure, 
Specialized bases, Smart Wheelchairs, Factors considered for selecting a 
9 

 
 
wheelchair, Safe transportation of individuals in wheelchairs. 
3 
Assistive Technologies for manipulation: Low-technology Aids for 
manipulation, Special-purpose electromechanical aids for manipulation, 
Electronic aids to daily living, Robotic aids - Principles of Assistive Robots, 
Robots as personal assistants, Mobile assistive robots, Robot use by children. 
Assistive Technologies for Vision: Reading aids, Optical and non-optical 
aids, Electronic aids, Braille displays, Recorded audio materials, Automatic 
reading of text, Mobility and orientation Aids – Canes, Alternative mobility 
devices, Electronic Travel Aids for Obstacle Detection, Orientation, and 
Mobility – Electronically augmented canes, Head-mounted glasses, 
Navigation aids for the blind – GPS-based, Special purpose visual aids.  
9 
4 
Assistive Technologies for hearing impaired and deaf: Hearing aids – 
Types – Body worn, Behind the ear, Spectacles aid, In the ear, Bone 
conduction, Middle ear implant, Cochlear implant, Auditory brain stem 
implant aids, Audio frequency induction loop systems, IR systems, Alarm 
and alerting devices – audio, visual and tactile alarms, Devices for deafblind 
– Braille devices, fingerprinting. Assistive Technologies for Cognitive 
Augmentation: Cognitive disorders – Congenital – Intellectual, learning, 
ADHD, Autism, Acquired disorders – Dementia, Brain injury, Stroke, 
Cognitive Assistive Technologies – Devices to aid memory, Time 
management, Prompting/Cueing/Coaching Devices. 
9

SEMESTER S7 
MEDICAL IMAGING TECHNIQUES 
Course Code 
OEEBT723 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course enables the students to understand the principle of image formation in various 
imaging modalities currently used in medicine. Students will be able to analyse the systems 
and techniques used in various diagnostic imaging methods. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
 1 
Ultrasound imaging: Properties of ultrasound- Doppler effect. Principle of 
image formation- constructional details of US probes- Transducer Design – 
Considerations-Transducer arrays- Modes of scanning-A mode-B mode-M 
mode 
scanners-Duplex 
scanning 
-instrumentation-axial 
and 
lateral 
resolutions-applications of each.    
 
9 
2 
Computed Tomography: Principle of CT imaging, Generations of 
scanners-system instrumentation-X-ray tubes for CT applications-pencil 
beam and cone beam projections-Image reconstruction algorithms for pencil 
beam, Image characteristics-CT numbers-  
 
9 
3 
Magnetic Resonance Imaging: Principle of Nuclear Magnetic Resonance-
Relaxation-MR instrumentation-Contrast mechanisms in MRI- pulse 
sequences- FLASH-GRASS-principle of image reconstruction,Spatial 
encoding systems-   k-space - Functional MRI- BOLD - Spatial and temporal 
Resolution of fMRI.    
9 
4 
Nuclear imaging-PET-SPECT-system level descriptions- Rectilinear 
Scanner, Gamma camera.  Hybrid Imaging: Instrumentation MR-PET 
Instrumentation-MR Compatible PET Detector Technology, MR-PET 
System Architecture. PET-CT, SPECT-CT.   
   
 
9

Course Objectives: 
1. Students will acquire knowledge in basic principles and designing of various types of 
artificial and tissue derived implants.

SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Cochlear implants: Basics of speech signal – Normal hearing mechanism – 
Deafness- Functional block diagram of cochlear implants-Implant 
characteristics & it’s classification -Auditory prostheses using deep brain 
stimulation-Physiological Challenges-Single-multiple source systems-Real 
time programming. 
9 
2

Pumping system-Kidney and it’s artificial replacement- Anatomy of skin - 
Design of artificial skin- Liver and it’s artificial replacement- ethical issues 
of implants. 
9 
3 
Micro electrode technologies for Deep Brain Stimulators (DBS): Implant 
site -Stimulation patterns - Closed loop control of DBS- Introduction to 
bionic micro stimulation-Clinical applications-Brain control and sensing of 
artificial limbs-Stimulation of peripheral nerve interfaces-Construction of 
implant-wireless communication-prosthetic master control unit. 
9 
4 
Fundamentals of Tissue Engineering: Engineering biomaterials for tissue 
9 

 
 
engineering- Nano biomaterials for tissue engineering – Drug delivery & 
Gene therapy mechanism- Vascularization of Engineered Tissues-Tissue  
engineering of nervous system & kidney (basic level). Fundamentals of 3 D 
printing and its applications in Biomedical engineering: Introduction of 
3D printing -3D printing process- Materials for 3D printing - Biomedical 
applications of 3 D printing technology- maxillofacial surgery & upper limb 
prosthetics.

SEMESTER S8 
TELEMEDICINE 
Course Code 
PEEBT861 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide an in-depth understanding of telemedicine systems, their components, and their 
evolution in healthcare. 
2. To analyze the communication technologies used in telemedicine, develop mHealth 
applications, and address data security, ethical issues, and implementation strategies, while 
exploring the broad applications of telemedicine in healthcare. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction of telemedicine: History of Telemedicine, Block diagram of 
telemedicine system, Definition of telemedicine, Tele health, Tele care, 
Origin & development of telemedicine, Scope, benefits and limitation of 
telemedicine. Global and Indian scenario. Telecommunication based 
biomedical 
systems 
Tele-radiology 
system, 
Tele-pathology, 
Tele- 
cardiology, Tele-oncology, Tele-surgery, Tele dermatology, Telemedicine in 
neurosciences Tele- education and Tele-Monitoring. 
9 
2 
 Types of Communication & networks: PSTN, POTS, ATN, ISDN, Internet 
and Wireless. Data communication networks-protocols and standards-
network models- the OSI model- layers in the OSI model- TCP/IP protocol 
suite- addressing- digital transmission- digital-to-digital conversion- analog-
to-digital conversion- transmission modes- switching- circuit-switched 
networks- virtual-circuit networks- structure of a switch- cryptography- 
symmetric-key cryptography- asymmetric-key cryptography- security 
services- 
message 
confidentiality-message 
integrity- 
Communication 
infrastructure for telemedicine – LAN and WAN technology. Data exchange 
Network Configuration, Circuit and packet switching, H.320 series (Video 
11 

 
 
phone-based ISBN) T.120, H.324 (Video phone based PSTN), Video 
Conferencing. 
3 
Introduction to mHealth Types of Health Apps Advantages and Benefits of 
Delivering Interventions via Health Apps Digital health interventions (DHIs) 
Application Development and Testing, Sensors and the Internet of Things 
(IoT). Smartphone and Microcontroller Communication – Mobile 
Computing for Remote Monitoring - Limitations of the Mobile and IoT 
Environment. 
9 
4 
Data security and standards& ethical and legal aspects of telemedicine Data 
security and standards: Standards to follow DICOM, HL 7, Ethical and legal 
aspects of telemedicine: Confidentiality and law, Patient rights and consent, 
access to medical records, consent treatment, intellectual property rights, 
jurisdictional issue. 
7

Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course aims to equip students with the knowledge and skills necessary to ensure that 
medical devices meet all relevant standards and regulatory requirements, ultimately 
enhancing patient safety and device performance. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Overview of Regulatory Landscape: 
Evolution of medical device regulation, General structure – benefits of 
regulation, Medical Device Nomenclature (GMDN / EMDN & Alternate 
Options), Global Harmonization – GHTF & IMDRF, RAPS.HTA overview– 
Clinical investigation of Medical Devices - Clinical investigation plan for 
Medical Devices; Good clinical practice for clinical investigation of medical 
devices (ISO 14155:2011); DHF Overview, GMP, Adverse event reporting 
of medical device. Medical Device Approval: Regulatory Bodies & Notified 
bodies, leading organizations. WHO Medical Devices: Global efforts, 
Ensuring 
availability, 
affordability 
and 
accessibility 
(Technical 
specifications and regulatory efforts). Overview: List of basic documents of 
National or State level importance for regulatory efforts / importance for 
Hospital Management, Summary Technical Document (STED). Indian 
regulatory organizational structure; Purpose and Functions; Working Groups 
9 
2 
Basic Regulatory Framework: Patient safety and risk management, Sterile 
/ Non-Sterile devices & packaging, Basics of classification of In vitro 
diagnostics & Medical Devices (active / non active). Regulatory approval 
process for Medical Devices: Comparison of US FDA, CE and Indian 
Medical device Rule; Device risk classification, Registration, Clinical trials, 
9 

 
 
Premarket Notification, Pre-Market Approval (PMA), Investigational Device 
Exemption (IDE) and In-vitro Diagnostics. 
3 
Advanced Regulatory Framework: Quality System Requirements: Quality 
management of Medical Devices - International Organization for 
Standardization, ISO 9001 - QMP Overview & Process Approach, ISO 
13485 (deeper understanding), ICMED 13485, ISO 14971 -Risk 
Management of Medical Devices, Unique Device Identification (UDI), 
Labelling requirements and Post market surveillance. 
9 
4 
Quality: Reliability, Product testing and Technical Standards: 
Reliability: HFE, MTBF, FMEA, FTA, Black box testing and white box 
testing, Environmental Stress Screening / Testing, Accelerated Life Testing 
Product/Materials testing: Biocompatibility, overview of ASTM, ISO 
Technical standards, Indian National standards other international standards. 
System / Sub System & Software testing standards: International 
Electrotechnical Commission (IEC-60601(1-2), Overview of 61010 & IEC 
62304 Compliances: RoHS, REACH, National level Safety testing’s for 
ionized radiations (for devices & Hospital installations). 
9

SEMESTER S8 
MECHATRONICS  
Course Code 
PEEBT863 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min 
Prerequisites (if any) 
GYEST104, 
GBEST213 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. The objective of this course is to get a basic idea about mechatronics – the working of 
differently powered systems as one unit and also to familiarize the mechanical actuators / 
mechanism and its electrical and electronic supporting systems and along with the application 
of mechatronic systems in industry. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Mechatronics 
Design 
System 
and 
Interfacing: 
Introduction 
to 
Mechatronics-Key elements of mechatronic systems. Functions of 
mechatronic systems. -Design approach- Properties of conventional and 
mechatronic design systems, Ways of integration. Concurrent design 
procedure for mechatronic systems. Examples of mechatronic systems. 
Mechatronic system interfacing: Input signals and output signals of a 
mechatronic System 
9 
2 
Actuation Systems: Pneumatic & hydraulic systems: process control valves, 
Directional and pressure control valves, Linear and rotary actuators.  
Mechanical Actuation Systems: Translational and Rotational motions, 
Kinematic Chains, Cams, Gear Trains, Ratchet and Pawl, Belt and Chain 
drives, Bearings. 
9 
3 
Electrical Actuation Systems, Performance characteristics and System 
modelling: Mechanical and solid-state relays, Solenoids, DC & AC motors, 
Servo & stepper motors. Sensors and transducers- Static and dynamic 
performance characteristics, Internal sensors, External sensors and 
microsensors. System modelling - Basic building blocks of general 
mechanical, electrical, fluid and thermal systems. 
9 

 
 
4 
Mechatronic System Controllers: Mechatronic System Controllers (basics 
only): ON/OFF, P, I, D, PI and PID Controllers, Digital controllers, 
Intelligent Controllers in Mechatronics. Fundamentals of numerical control - 
advantages of NC systems- classification of NC systems - point to point and 
contouring systems - NC and CNC - incremental and absolute systems -open 
loop and closed loop systems. 
Basics of Programmable Logic Controller and Industrial Robotics 
Programmable Logic Controller- Basic PLC structure, I/O processing. 
Industrial robotics - basic concepts - robot anatomy - robotics and 
automation - specification of robots - resolution - repeatability and accuracy 
of manipulator - classification of robots. 
9

SEMESTER S8 
REHABILITATION ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PEEBT864 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs.30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Students will acquire knowledge in basic principles of orthoses and assistive devices and 
design of features of nerve stimulators. 
2. Students will be able to understand features and principles of rehabilitation methods and its 
applications. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Orthoses and assistive devices: Introduction, Participatory Action Design, 
Policy, Human, Activity, assistance, Technology, and environment 
(PHAATE) Model, Telerehabilitation, Service Delivery Models, Principles 
of service delivery - Orthoses for spinal dysfunction-three column concept 
function-cervicothoracic and thoracic orthoses-thoracolumbar-lumbosacral-
scoliosis-kinds of loading calculation of bending moments-treatment 
methods- Powered wheel chairs- multi functional wheel chairs- regulations 
and standards-micro controller based wheel chairs -design features-smart 
wheel chairs. 
9 
2 
Electrical Stimulation (ES) Devices: Clinical Considerations of ES- 
Neuromuscular stimulation (NMS) of atrophied muscles, Foot drop and 
Wrist drop, Electrodes- Transcutaneous, Subcutaneous and Percutaneous 
electrodes, Spinal Cord Stimulation (SCS) and Deep Brain Stimulation 
(DBS). Clinical Applications- ES for Foot Drop, Ultralow power Electronics 
for SCS & DBS-Biomimetic design of neural prostheses-tissue device 
interface-neuro modulation through stimulation-sensory restoration motor 
9 

 
 
restoration-integrated neural prostheses. 
3 
Auditory and Visual Aid Devices : Types of hearing impairment, Hearing 
function assessment, Hearing assistance technology solutions, Surgical 
approaches- Middle-ear implants (MEIs) and bone anchored hearing aids 
(BAHAs), Non-surgical - Hearing Aids Assistive Listening Solutions, Voice 
synthesizer and speech trainer-Types of visual impairments, Visual function 
assessment, Assistive Technology- Medical/ Surgical Techniques, Cortical 
Implants, Retinal Implants, Optic-Nerve Stimulation, Auditory and tactile 
information display, Blind Mobility Aids, GPS Technology, Audible and 
Remotely Readable Signs 
9 
4 
Neural 
Rehabilitation: 
Neural 
repair 
and 
rehabilitation-outcome 
measurement and diagnostic technology- Electromyography - neuro imaging 
–rehabilitation in chronic pain-loss of somatic sensation- gait disorders and 
rehabilitation-balance, vestibular and occulomotor dysfunction-rehabilitation 
of stroke- brain response to neural prostheses. 
Robotic assistive Technologies: Use of robots in rehabilitation-international 
safety Standards-Challenges- Human robot interaction for rehabilitation 
robots-types of information exchange-HRI matics-physical & social HRI-
Assistive Robotic Manipulators (ARM)-Functions-Requirements-Upper limb 
and lower limb robotic robotic prostheses-challenges and benefits-
components-in corporation with human body.  
9

SEMESTER S8 
MEDICAL INFORMATICS 
 
Course Code 
PEEBT866 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs.30 Min 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course is designed to offer an in-depth understanding of health informatics, 
blending theoretical frameworks, models, and practical applications within healthcare 
systems. 
2. Students will explore key concepts including electronic health records (EHRs), 
telehealth, health information exchange, and healthcare analytics. 
 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Overview of health informatics: Definition of health informatics, Theories 
& models underlying health informatics-Systems Theory, Chaos’s Theory, 
Complexity Theory, Information Theory, Diffusion of innovation theory, 
Learning Theory, Change Theory, System Life cycle models, Staggers & 
Nelson system Life cycle model, Evidence based practice & Informatics-
Evidence based practice models, ACE star model of knowledge 
transformation. 
9 
2 
Information system in healthcare delivery: Electronic health Records– 
Definition, Electronic medical Record versus Electronic Health Record, 
EHR: components, Functions & Attributes, EHR applications used in clinical 
settings, benefits, Barriers to EHR adoption. Telehealth & Applications for 
9 

 
 
delivering care at a distance–Technologies, Clinical Practice considerations 
for healthcare professionals, Operational & Organizational success factors & 
barriers, Telehealth challenges, Clinical Decision support system in Health 
care. 
3 
Health information exchange & health care analytics: Health information 
exchange-Basic definitions, The Nationwide Health Information Network 
(NHIN) and, NHIN Exchange &NHIN Direct, Health Information 
Organizations (HIOs), Federal Gateway Overview, Web Services and 
Service 
Oriented 
Architecture, 
Healthcare 
Analytics-Introduction, 
Components of healthcare analytics, Tools: SQL (basics)-SQLite, Python 
Features-Lists and tuples, Dictionaries, Sets, Python libraries- pandas and 
scikit-learn- Linear regression model, Logistic Regression 
9 
4 
Healthcare security: Patient medical Information-Privacy, Confidentiality, 
Security-Definition, Legal & historical context, Principles, laws & 
Regulations, Use of ICT in healthcare. Bioinformatics & mobile 
computing in health care: Basics for Bioinformatics- Cells, DNA and 
Chromosome, the Central Dogma, Genes and the Genome, DNA 
Sequencing, Transcriptomics and DNA Microarrays, Proteomics and Mass 
Spectrometer, ChIP-Chip and ChIP-Seq, Basic Principles of Genetics-
Mendel and Morgan’s Legacy, Disease Gene Mapping in the Genomic Era. 
9

SEMESTER S8 
MODELLING OF PHYSIOLOGICAL SYSTEMS 
Course Code 
PEEBT865 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs.30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Quantitative approaches to understand various physiological systems is introduced. 
2.  Enable the student to understand the basic concepts of mathematical analysis of transport 
mechanisms across cell membranes, propagation of impulse, processes in respiratory systems, 
cardiac electrophysiology, and computational aspects of neuronal models. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Modeling approaches in physiological systems: Physiological complexity 
and need for models, Feedback and control in physiological systems. 
Modeling process-steps, Different approaches in system modeling- 
parametric 
and 
nonparametric 
modeling, 
linear 
and 
nonlinear, 
compartmental modeling. (Examples of each type in physiological system).   
9 
2 
Mathematical analysis of cardiac physiology: Basic Cardiac Anatomy and 
Electro cardiology Conduction System: The Electrocardiogram (ECG) 
Cardiac Action Potential Models, Biophysical models Noble-Noble models, 
reduced cell models. Mathematical models of Cardiac Cells Arrangements: 
The Bidomain and monodomain models.  
9 
3 
Mathematical models of computational neuroscience: Electrophysiology 
of neurons, Ionic currents and conductance, Equivalent circuit representation 
of a patch of cell membrane, resting membrane potential, voltage-gated 
channels, Hodgkin–Huxley model formulation for action potential, 
Compartmental models, Simplified models of neurons Integrate-and-fire 
neurons Spike-response model neurons Rate-based models  
9 
4 
Dynamical systems in physiology: Dynamical system analysis- Types of 
fixed points, Phase plane analysis - nullclines - Hopf bifurcation and limit 
cycles. van der Pol oscillator, Fitzhugh Nagumo model Phase-plane analysis, 
9 

 
 
showing excitability, bistability and oscillations. Simulation studies of 
simplified models (Eg. Izhikevich neuron models) 
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5

10 
10 
40 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
Criteria for evaluation: 
1. Problem Definition (K4 - 5 points) 
a. Clearly defines the problem. 
b. Examine and identifies relevant factors. 
2. Problem Analysis (K4 - 5 points) 
a. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
3. Evaluate (K5 - 5 points) 
a. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
4. Conclusion (K3- 3 points, K5 – 2 points) 
a. Summarizes findings and insights. State which solution is most appropriate 
for the problem 
Scoring: 
1. Accomplished (4 points): Exceptional analysis, and depth of understanding. 
2. Competent (3 points): Solid performance with minor areas for improvement. 
3. Developing (2 points): Adequate effort but lacks depth or clarity. 
4. Minimal (1 point): Incomplete or significantly flawed.

SEMESTER S8 
IOT & BIOMEDICAL APPLICATIONS 
Course Code 
OEEBT831 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. Develop a comprehensive understanding of Internet of Things (IoT) concepts, including 
key protocols, architectural principles, and sensor technologies, with a focus on their 
theoretical applications and implications. 
2. Examine the various IoT protocols and architectures, understanding their roles and 
interactions within IoT ecosystems, and evaluating their effectiveness in different 
contexts. 
3. Explore the theoretical aspects of wearable health monitoring systems, including their 
design, functionality, and integration with data analytics and cloud technologies to 
address healthcare challenges. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to IoT and Enabling Technologies:  Introduction to Internet 
of Things – Definition and Characteristics of IoT, Physical Design of IoT – 
IoT Protocols, Logical Design of IoT - IoT communication models, IoT 
Communication APIs. IoT enabled Technologies - Wireless Sensor 
Networks, Cloud Computing, Embedded Systems. Sensor Interfaces – ECG, 
EEG, PPG, Pulse Oximeter, Temperature Sensors, and Pressure Sensors. 
Challenges of using IoT in Healthcare. 
9 
2 
IoT Protocols, Architecture, and Standards: IoT Protocols & 
Architecture: Protocols - Protocol Standardization for IoT – Efforts – M2M 
and WSN Protocols – SCADA and RFID Protocols – Issues with IoT 
Standardization – Unified Data Standards – IEEE802.15.4 – BACNet 
Protocol – Modbus – KNX – Zigbee. Network and Security Architecture. 
IoT Open Source Architecture (OIC) - OIC Architecture & Design 
9 

 
 
Principles. IoT Devices and Deployment Models - IoTivity: An Open-source 
IoT Stack - Overview - IoTivity Stack Architecture - Resource Model and 
Abstraction. 
3 
Wearable Health Monitoring Systems and IoT Implementation: 
Wearable Health Monitoring System (WHMS): Basics of WHMS, Need for 
Wearable Systems, Applications of WHMS - Home Healthcare, 
Sports/Fitness. Design of Wearables: Introduction, Architecture, and 
Attributes. Design of Smart Textiles and Wearable Electronics. Issues of 
WHMS & Factors Inhibiting Growth. Building IoT with Arduino & 
Raspberry Pi: Programming – Python Program with Raspberry Pi, 
Controlling Hardware - Controlling AC Power Devices with Relays, 
Controlling Servo Motor, DC Motor. Sensors - Light Sensor, Motion 
Detection Sensors, Wireless Bluetooth Sensors. 
9 
4 
Data Handling, Analytics, and Cloud for IoT: Data Handling & Analytics: 
Introduction, Big Data, Types of Data, Characteristics of Big Data, Data 
Handling Technologies, Data Acquisition, Data Storage. Introduction to Data 
Analytics, Types of Data Analytics, Local Analytics, Cloud Analytics, and 
Applications. IoT Physical Servers and Cloud Offerings – Introduction to 
Cloud Storage Models and Communication APIs. Webserver – Web Server 
for IoT, Cloud for IoT, Python Web Application Framework, Designing a 
RESTful Web API. 
9

SEMESTER S8 
HUMAN FACTORS IN ENGINEERING AND DESIGN  
Course Code 
OEEBT832 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the basic concepts and techniques employed in broad area of human factors 
engineering focusing on anthropometric principles in design of work places and to optimize 
the interaction between human and systems. 
2. Integrate human factor considerations in the design of medical devices and health care tools 
for improved user experience and safety. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Introduction to Human factors Engineering – Definition, Human Factors 
& Systems - Aspects of Human-machine systems.  A model of Human 
information 
processing. 
Process 
of 
seeing- 
Visual 
capabilities- 
Accommodation, Visual acuity and Contrast sensitivity. Factors affecting 
visual capabilities. Human factor aspects of hard copy text and computer 
screen text. Graphic representations of Text & Data. Human factors in 
designing Symbols & Codes 
    9 
2 
Visual Displays - Qualitative visual displays, Quantitative visual displays, 
Signals & Warning lights, Representational Displays-Aircraft Bank Angle 
displays-Principles of aircraft position displays.  Auditory Displays - 
Process of hearing. Principles of auditory displays, Auditory Displays for 
Specific Purposes. Cutaneous Senses- Tactual Displays-, Substitute for 
Hearing, seeing, Tactual graph. Compatibility – Types of Compatibility-
Conceptual, movement, spatial and Modality Compatibility. Movement 
compatibility- Rotary controls and rotary displays in same plane and 
different plane.  
      9 

 
 
       3 
Muscle Physiology- Work Physiology. Measure of physiological strain, 
Physical Workload, Strength & Endurance. Manual Material Handling 
(MMH), Bio-mechanical recommended limits of MMH. Reducing the risk of 
MMH overexertion. General principles of Biomechanical Design. 
Anthropometry -Anthropometric design principles. Static and Dynamic 
Anthropometry. Case study of Anthropometric Design- Viewing Angle 
determination of Cardiac Output Monitor. Work place and Seating Design-
Work space envelope, Factors in design of workspace surfaces, Principles of 
seat design. 
     9 
4 
 Classification of human errors-Dealing with human errors. Accidents - 
Theories of accident causation-CFAC model. Occupational Safety and 
Health - Industrial Safety and Health, Hazards and Control Measures, 
Warnings and Safety Programs. Human factors for Mobile medical device 
design - General and special considerations, Design principles for home 
healthcare; Consideration related to Hand tool design in health care. Case 
studies exemplifying design for device mobility and use in motion: Infusion 
pumps, Portable X-Ray machine, Portable Ultrasound Device, Transport 
ventilator. 
      9

SEMESTER S8 
MEDICAL IMAGE PROCESSING 
 
Course Code 
OEEBT833 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide an overview of the nature of human visual perception, the elements of an image-
processing system which includes sampling, quantisation and two dimensional transforms. 
2. To make the students familiar with image enhancement, restoration, segmentation, 
classification, machine learning and deep learning techniques for image analysis. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours
1 
Image perception -MTF of the visual system –monochrome vision models - 
color vision model. Image sampling and quantization: Two-dimensional 
sampling theory, Image quantization - uniform quantizer. Image transforms -
Two dimensional orthogonal and unitary transforms - properties of unitary 
transforms, 2D DFT, DCT, Hadamard, Haar, KL transforms. 
9 
2 
Image enhancement: contrast enhancement, clipping and thresholding - 
digital negative, intensity level slicing - bit extraction. Histogram processing, 
Magnification and interpolation. Image Enhancement in Spatial domain: 
Smoothing and sharpening operations in time domain, Filtering in frequency 
domain: Smoothing and sharpening frequency domain filters, Homomorphic 
filtering. 
9 
3 
Image restoration: Image degradation, Noise, Blurring, Modelling image 
degradation, Inverse filtering, Wiener filtering. Image segmentation- 
Thresholding- optimal, adaptive, Region-based methods- region growing and 
region merging, Boundary-based methods- edge detection and linking, 
9 

 
 
boundary tracking. 
4 
Feature recognition and classification: Features - describing the contents 
and the shape of objects. Classification- Supervised and unsupervised 
learning. Discriminant analysis, k-nearest-Neighbor (kNN) classifier. 
Unsupervised- k-means clustering. Deep Learning for Medical Image 
Analysis, Convolutional Neural Networks. Image fusion for hybrid imaging, 
Super resolution imaging. 
9

Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Students will be able to review the principles and design features of orthoses, assistive 
devices, nerve stimulators, and technical aspects of audio and visual rehabilitation measures. 
2. Students can acquire knowledge of neural rehabilitation methods and explore the applications 
of robots in assistive technologies. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Orthoses and assistive devices: Introduction, Participatory Action Design, 
Policy, Human, Activity, assistance, Technology, and environment 
(PHAATE) Model, Telerehabilitation, Service Delivery Models, Principles 
of service delivery - Orthoses for spinal dysfunction-three column concept 
function-cervicothoracic and thoracic orthoses-thoracolumbar-lumbosacral-
scoliosis-kinds of loading calculation of bending moments-treatment 
methods- Powered wheel chairs- multi functional wheel chairs- regulations 
and standards-micro controller based wheel chairs -design features-smart 
wheel chairs. 
9 
2 
Electrical Stimulation (ES) Devices: Clinical Considerations of ES- 
Neuromuscular stimulation (NMS) of atrophied muscles, Foot drop and 
Wrist drop, Electrodes- Transcutaneous, Subcutaneous and Percutaneous 
electrodes, Spinal Cord Stimulation (SCS) and Deep Brain Stimulation 
(DBS). Clinical Applications- ES for Foot Drop, Ultralow power Electronics 
for SCS & DBS-Biomimetic design of neural prostheses-tissue device 
9 

 
 
interface-neuro modulation through stimulation-sensory restorationmotor 
restoration-integrated neural prostheses. 
3 
Auditory and Visual Aid Devices : Types of hearing impairment, Hearing 
function assessment, Hearing assistance technology solutions, Surgical 
approaches- Middle-ear implants (MEIs) and bone anchored hearing aids 
(BAHAs), Non-surgical - Hearing Aids Assistive Listening Solutions, Voice 
synthesizer and speech trainer-Types of visual impairments, Visual function 
assessment, Assistive Technology- Medical/ Surgical Techniques, Cortical 
Implants, Retinal Implants, Optic-Nerve Stimulation, Auditory and tactile 
information display, Blind Mobility Aids, GPS Technology, Audible and 
Remotely Readable Signs 
9 
4 
Neural 
Rehabilitation: 
Neural 
repair 
and 
rehabilitation-outcome 
measurement and diagnostic technology- Electromyography - neuro imaging 
–rehabilitation in chronic pain-loss of somatic sensation- gait disorders and 
rehabilitation-balance, vestibular and occulomotor dysfunction-rehabilitation 
of stroke- brain response to neural prostheses. Robotic assistive 
Technologies: Use of robots in rehabilitation-international safety Standards-
Challenges- Human robot interaction for rehabilitation robots-types of 
information exchange-HRI matics-physical & social HRI-Assistive Robotic 
Manipulators (ARM)-Functions-Requirements-Upper limb and lower limb 
robotic 
robotic 
prostheses-challenges 
and 
benefits-components-in 
corporation with human body.
